He had been gone for three weeks, part of a delegation of three hundred provincial representatives summoned to greet the King after the subjugation of the Orrenese Lattice. Rogr was a good man\u2014a textile merchant with a gift for smoothing over trade disputes, which is why the local magistrate had chosen him. He left with a pressed tunic and a nervous smile, proud to serve the Crown. He returned eight hours before his scheduled arrival, stumbling through the door with the glaze of a man who had walked through a slaughterhouse.\n\nHis pupils were pinned. His skin, normally warm cedar, had turned the gray of wet ash. When I touched his cheek, he flinched so violently he nearly knocked over the dining table. Our son Pete, seven at the time, rushed to hug his father\u2019s legs, and Rogr made a noise\u2014a strangled, high-pitched note through clenched teeth\u2014and then he did something that still knots my stomach. He shoved. He shoved Pete hard enough that the boy skidded across the floor, and then Rogr collapsed into the corner of the room, covering his head with his arms, whispering \u201cNo, no, no, please\u201d in a voice that had been dragged over broken glass.\n\nThat was the beginning. Ten years ago. And in those ten years, I never understood what he carried. Not really. Not until I saw the thing that had cursed him undo it with less effort than a man blinks.\n\nBut I\u2019m getting ahead. You need to understand what it was like living in the shadow of his affliction, in a kingdom that knew only perfection.\n\nKing Godric\u2019s rule was, by any measure, a paradise. Under the Awakening, every man past the age of twenty grew stronger, smarter, more capable with each passing day. My husband, before that ceremony, had been among them\u2014a quiet, sturdy man who could lift a wagon with one hand when he needed to, though he usually suppressed it to avoid unsettling his customers. The streets in our town of Halden\u2019s Reach were clean, the air sweet with the scent of the flowering vines that draped the public buildings. Women walked alone at any hour because the King\u2019s decree protected them absolutely; a man who so much as frightened a woman would find himself facing a judgment so swift and final that no one ever considered it. Crime didn\u2019t exist. Hunger was a story from old books.\n\nEveryone loved the King. I loved the King. He was the father we had never known, the shield against an increasingly chaotic cosmos. My son Pete grew up with a painted portrait of Godric in his schoolroom, and every morning he would salute it before his lessons. He wasn\u2019t unusual. It was common to hear spontaneous cheers for the King in the market square, just because someone mentioned his name. I took part in those cheers.\n\nAnd yet, my husband reacted to the King\u2019s name the way a rabbit reacts to the shadow of a hawk. When the town crier announced a new decree, Rogr would freeze mid-sentence, his eyes focusing on a point a thousand yards away. The sound of a distant ceremonial cannonade\u2014common on the King\u2019s birthday\u2014sent him into a gasping fit that once lasted an hour. At night, he screamed. Not words, just a noise that started in the base of his spine and ripped upward, pure terror given voice. I held him through those nights, pressing my chest to his back, whispering that he was safe, that whatever he saw wasn\u2019t here. But he could never tell me what it was. When I asked, he would shake his head, a muscle in his jaw jumping, and say, \u201cYou wouldn\u2019t believe me, Rosa. You\u2019d think I was mad. Maybe I am.\u201d\n\nI tried everything. That\u2019s not an exaggeration\u2014I tried *everything* that a merchant\u2019s wife with savings and a desperate love could conceive.\n\nThe first specialist was a renowned psycho-surgeon from the capital. She placed her palms on Rogr\u2019s temples and initiated a standard memory-smoothing protocol. The moment her consciousness touched the fringes of whatever black knot sat in his mind, she shrieked and fell backward, blood jetting from her nostrils. She died three days later of a full neurological cascade\u2014all her nerves had fired simultaneously until her body simply cooked from within. The Coroner\u2019s report said \u201cunexplained resonance.\u201d\n\nI found a wisewoman who claimed to brew a tea that could quiet the deepest fears. When she handed the steaming cup to Rogr, the liquid curdled instantly into a foul, black sludge that ate through the ceramic and burned a hole in the wooden table. The wisewoman fled and never returned.\n\nA cult called the Children of the Unseen Word operated in the lower quarter. They believed that exposure to the King\u2019s divine radiance could heal any ailment. I took Rogr to one of their rituals\u2014a secret affair in a basement, with chanting and a stolen fragment of a banner that had supposedly touched the King\u2019s palace. As the chanting reached a pitch and the fragment glowed, the air in the room thickened until it was hard to breathe. Then, soundlessly, the cult leader\u2019s eyes burst. The other participants clutched their heads and screamed in a language I didn\u2019t know. The banner fragment flared white and disintegrated. Rogr, who had been catatonic throughout, simply sat there, unharmed, while the room descended into chaos. I dragged him out as people clawed at their faces.\n\nI visited an Awakened sage who had, by the age of seventy-eight, accumulated the wisdom of a million lifetimes. He listened patiently, then attempted to weave a mental shield over Rogr. The shield held for twelve seconds before it inverted and began feeding the sage\u2019s own deepest terrors back into his brain. He clawed out his left eye before he deactivated the spell. As I apologized, he fixed me with a gaze of raw, sane horror. \u201cWoman,\u201d he rasped, \u201cyour husband has touched something that should not be touched. It is not of this plane. It is not of any plane. I cannot help you.\u201d\n\nMonths bled into years. Our savings dwindled. Pete grew into a lanky, earnest boy who no longer tried to hug his father because Rogr would always tense like a drawn bowstring. Instead, Pete showed his love by sitting nearby, reading aloud from the official histories, recounting the glorious conquests of Thronegate under King Godric. I saw Rogr\u2019s knuckles whiten every time the King\u2019s name was spoken, but Pete didn\u2019t notice. He worshiped Godric with a fervor that bordered on religious. It wasn\u2019t his fault\u2014how could he understand?\n\nBy the tenth year, I had stopped trying to cure Rogr. Instead, I tried to build a quiet routine around the trembling. I learned to speak softly, to avoid sudden movements. Our house became a bubble of careful silences.\n\nAnd then I opened the door to a stranger with a friendly muttonchop beard and the weight of a galaxy on his shoulders.\n\nHe introduced himself as Blake, Court Wizard to King Godric. My first instinct was to drop to one knee, but he held up a hand with a tired smile. \u201cPlease don\u2019t. I\u2019m just a man. And I\u2019ve come to apologize.\u201d\n\nI let him in, bewildered. He stood in the hallway, not sitting, and for a moment he just looked at me as if measuring the depth of my fatigue. Then he told me a story. He spoke of a man named Godric who, long ago, had been a kind king. He spoke of a joke he, Blake, had suggested: that when the delegates from the conquered universes arrived with their expectations of a cruel tyrant, Godric could humor them by playing the part for a few moments before revealing his true nature. Just a harmless prank among friends.\n\n\u201cI thought it would be funny,\u201d Blake said, his voice cracking. \u201cYou have to understand, Godric trusts me more than anyone. He\u2019s\u2026 he\u2019s not good at gauging mortals anymore. When he gets an idea, he runs with it. So when those delegates entered the throne room, he aimed the tiniest fraction of a displeased thought at them. Just a whisper of a frown. A sliver. He thought it would be amusing to see them squirm for a second, then he\u2019d laugh and welcome them.\u201d\n\nI stared at him. \u201cA sliver.\u201d\n\n\u201cYes. He held back everything else. He said afterward, \u2018They\u2019ll be fine, they just need to tough it out. Mortals are resilient.\u2019 And then we forgot about it. We forgot about it, Rosa, because we are blind, stupid, privileged\u2026\u201d He trailed off, rubbing his face. \u201cA few days ago, I was playing chess with Godric. He moved a pawn and said, idly, \u2018That delegate from Halden\u2019s Reach, the one who still hasn\u2019t recovered\u2014remarkable how some people can\u2019t bounce back.\u2019 I didn\u2019t know what he meant at first. Then he explained. He has absolute omniscience, you see. He knew about your husband\u2019s condition from the moment it happened. But he genuinely believed Rogr would overcome it with time. He respected that struggle, in his way. He didn\u2019t want to interfere because he thought it would be condescending. He said, \u2018Mortal resilience is a thing of beauty.\u2019\u201d\n\nThe rage that filled me then was so hot I thought I might attack the Court Wizard. But it wasn\u2019t his fault, not entirely. And besides, he was here, trembling, his own guilt a raw wound. So I swallowed the fire and asked, \u201cWhy are you telling me this now?\u201d\n\n\u201cBecause I\u2019ve come to ask your permission,\u201d he said. \u201cI yelled at him. I\u2026 I said things to my King I shouldn\u2019t have, but he listened. And he\u2019s agreed to fix it, if you and Rogr wish it. I won\u2019t have him do anything without your consent.\u201d\n\nI left him in the hall and went to the bedroom where Rogr sat staring at the wall. I knelt in front of my husband and took his hands. They were cold. \u201cA man is here,\u201d I said. \u201cHe can make the bad thing go away. Do you want that?\u201d\n\nRogr\u2019s eyes focused on me for the first time in years. There was a flicker of the man I married. \u201cThe King?\u201d he whispered, and the word was both prayer and curse.\n\n\u201cThe King.\u201d\n\nPete, who had been listening at the door, burst in. \u201cMother, is that\u2014is that the Court Wizard? He serves King Godric! This is an honor! Father, you must accept! Please!\u201d\n\nRogr flinched at Pete\u2019s voice, but then he looked at his son, really looked. Something passed between them. Rogr\u2019s jaw tightened, and he nodded once, a jerky motion.\n\nI led him into the hall. Blake stood with his back against the wall, looking far older than his years. \u201cWe accept,\u201d I said.\n\nAnd in that instant, the room changed.\n\nI can only describe it as a presence that was not a presence, a weight that pressed on the fabric of existence without being heavy. The air didn\u2019t move, but I felt it watching, considering. Then, between one heartbeat and the next, he was there. King Godric, of Olympus-Secundus, ruler of the omniverse, stood in my hallway.\n\nHe was a tall man, broad-shouldered, with a salt-and-pepper beard and short, steel-gray hair. His build spoke of immense physical power, but his face\u2026 his face was gentle. He wore simple clothes, a dark blue tunic and worn boots. He looked like a kindly father, not the god of gods. Yet my knees buckled. Pete, beside me, was weeping openly, not from fear but from awe. Rogr made a small sound, a whimper I had heard a thousand times, and tried to retreat.\n\nGodric raised a hand\u2014not menacingly, just to halt him. \u201cDon\u2019t be afraid,\u201d he said, and his voice was low and warm, the kind of voice that could read bedtime stories. \u201cIt was my fault. I apologize, truly. I forget sometimes how thin the line is.\u201d\n\nHe didn\u2019t gesture or speak any incantation. He didn\u2019t even seem to concentrate. He just looked at Rogr, and Rogr straightened. It was like watching a crumpled leaf be smoothed out by an invisible hand. Color flushed into his cheeks. The permanent tension in his shoulders dissolved. His eyes, which for a decade had been the color of old bruises, brightened to a clear brown I hadn\u2019t seen since our wedding day. He took a sudden, deep breath, and it was the first full breath I\u2019d seen him take in years.\n\n\u201cWhat\u2026?\u201d Rogr said, and his voice was steady. Strong. \u201cI\u2014I\u2019m hungry. Rosa, I\u2019m actually hungry.\u201d\n\nPete surged forward and wrapped his arms around his father, and this time Rogr didn\u2019t flinch. He laughed\u2014a sound so strange I\u2019d forgotten he could make it\u2014and he hugged his son back.\n\nI stood frozen, my mind a storm. Ten years. Ten years of sleepless nights, of watching my husband dissolve into a shell, of spending every coin and every scrap of energy on cures that ended in blood and ruin. And he did it. He did it without moving, without trying, as if he were swatting a fly that had been buzzing too long. The sheer, merciless *ease* of it clawed at my chest. I wanted to scream. I wanted to throw myself at his feet and thank him. I did both, inside, and the conflicting impulses made me shake so hard that I had to brace myself against the wall.\n\nGodric turned his attention to me, and his smile was kind. \u201cRosa of Halden\u2019s Reach. You have suffered much. I would offer you compensation\u2014whatever you desire. A palace of woven starlight on a private moon. A hundred thousand years of prosperity for your bloodline. A fragment of cosmic insight that would make you a living oracle. Name it, and it is yours.\u201d\n\nIt was an astronomical overpayment. Any of those things would have elevated us beyond the wildest dreams of anyone in the galaxy. And the chilling part was that I knew, in my bones, that he meant it. These treasures were nothing to him. Less than nothing. I could have asked for the throne of a universe and he would have granted it with the same warmth.\n\nBut I didn\u2019t want it. I didn\u2019t want anything that would cheapen those ten years of horror. If I accepted, it would mean the suffering was just a transaction, a price to be paid and refunded. So I shook my head. \u201cYour Majesty, I only ever wanted my husband back. You have given me that. I need nothing more.\u201d\n\nHe nodded, and there was no surprise in his expression. \u201cAs you wish. Your strength does you credit, Rosa.\u201d He laid a hand on Blake\u2019s shoulder. \u201cThis one was right to scold me. Thank you for allowing me to make amends, even a little.\u201d\n\nAnd then they left, or prepared to. I walked them to the door because it felt wrong not to. My legs were still wobbling, but I needed to see them go, to let the house settle back into its own shape. They descended the front steps into the twilight, and I stood in the doorway, the cool air on my face.\n\nThat\u2019s when I heard it.\n\nGodric\u2019s voice, a low rumble of amusement, drifted back through the evening. \u201cYou know, Blake, that went rather well. It gave me an idea. Next delegation, perhaps I should try being a mad jester. I could make the walls bleed candy. Just for a moment. The reaction would be priceless.\u201d\n\nBlake\u2019s reply was a strangled groan. \u201cAbsolutely not. No more pranks. Never again. I am ordering you, as your friend\u2014no more.\u201d\n\nGodric chuckled, a sound that in any other context would be jovial. \u201cBut you planted the original seed, my friend. It\u2019s tradition now.\u201d\n\n\u201cI will burn every seed,\u201d Blake said darkly.\n\nTheir conversation faded as they walked down the road. I stayed in the doorway, my hand gripping the frame, my heart a knot of conflicting emotions. I loved my King. He had restored my husband, and for that I would carve his name into my soul. But the ease of it, and the casual way he spoke of toying with the next group of delegates, sent a tremor through the foundations of my world. I saw, in that moment, the truth that everyone in Thronegate knew but rarely acknowledged: we lived at the pleasure of a being who existed so far above us that our reality was his canvas, our trauma was a fleeting whim, and our resilience was a curiosity to be admired and, occasionally, tweaked for his friends\u2019 entertainment.\n\nI turned back inside. Rogr was laughing with Pete, his face alive in a way that made my heart sing. I joined them, and I smiled, and I meant it. We were safe. We were blessed. The King was good.\n\nAnd yet, late that night, when the house was still and Rogr\u2019s breathing was deep and peaceful beside me, I stared at the ceiling and felt the weight of that cosmic imbalance press down on my chest. I loved Godric. I would follow him into any abyss. But a part of me, a small, terrified part, now understood what my husband had been trying to articulate for ten years: to be noticed by a god, even kindly, is to be unmade.\n\nTomorrow, I would go to the temple and light a candle of thanks. And I would mean it. The cognitive dissonance was a price I would pay willingly. Because the alternative was unthinkable, and besides, the King had said my name, and in that memory there was a terrifying, holy sweetness.\n\nI closed my eyes and waited for dawn.\n\n---\n\n**Now let's check the word count.** This draft is about 1500 words. Need to nearly double. Let's expand certain sections with more visceral detail, more attempts at curing Rogr, more internal monologue.\n\n**Expand the attempted cures section:** Add more examples with gore and horror. That can be graphic.\n- More failed attempts: maybe she tries a technological solution from an off-world scientist that backfires catastrophically. Maybe she seeks a legendary artifact from a conquered universe, only to have it crumble.\n- The family dynamics: Pete's idolization of Godric leading to arguments. He had been chosen as one of three hundred provincial delegates\u2014a minor honor, really, a way for the Crown to include the common folk in the pageantry of conquest. He was to stand in the Throne Room of the Resplendent Spire and present a bolt of our district\u2019s finest weave as a token of fealty. Simple. He practiced his bow for a week.\n\nHe returned on foot, with no escort, his tunic untucked and stained. The first thing I noticed was the smell: a cold, metallic scent clinging to him, like the air after a lightning strike. His eyes were wide and unfocused, the pupils so dilated they looked like pools of oil. When I touched his arm, he didn\u2019t flinch\u2014at first. Then he blinked, looked at me, and his face crumpled into an expression of such raw, infantile terror that I stumbled back.\n\n\u201cRogr?\u201d I said.\n\nHe opened his mouth, but no words came. Just a croak that spiraled into a whimper. He walked past me into the house, his gait unsteady, and he found the corner of our bedroom\u2014the angle where two walls met\u2014and he wedged himself in, his back to the plaster, and he pulled a chair in front of him like a barricade. He stayed there for three days, only moving to drink water when I pressed the cup to his lips.\n\nI asked the other delegates\u2019 families later. A dozen of them had similar stories\u2014husbands, wives, sons who came back hollowed out, unable to sleep, plagued by nightmares that made them scream until their throats bled. Three of them ended their own lives within the first month. The official explanation was a \u201cpsychic overload\u201d from the celestial energies of the subjugated universe. It was a lie, but I didn\u2019t know that then.\n\nRogr was one of the ones who survived. Survived, if you can call it that. Over the next decade, I watched the man I married\u2014the man who could laugh until the windows rattled, who could cook a fourteen-course meal just to see my smile\u2014dissolve into a creature of endless, silent dread. He could no longer work; the slightest noise\u2014a dropped pot, a child\u2019s shout\u2014would send him into a catatonic state that lasted hours. He stopped speaking in full sentences. His affectionate touches vanished; he would let me hold him, but he never initiated, and his skin always felt cool, like he was slowly turning to stone from the inside.\n\nPete was seven when it started. He didn\u2019t understand. How could he? His world was a kingdom of flawless order, a kingdom where the King was the sun and the rest of us were planets basking in his light. Pete grew up believing, as all children did, that King Godric was the absolute epitome of good. And that belief only hardened as he grew older and saw the city prosper, saw the Awakening transform his uncles and neighbors into veritable heroes. By the time he was fifteen, he could recite the King\u2019s declarations from memory. He would come home from school buzzing with news of another universe that had been offered mercy and refused; and then, in history class, they\u2019d analyze how the Thronegate legions had triumphantly brought the misguided populace into the fold within the span of a lunch break. The pride in his voice made Rogr shake.\n\nI tried to bridge that gap. I sat Pete down once, when he was maybe thirteen, and told him that his father was ill because of something that happened at the King\u2019s ceremony. Pete\u2019s brow furrowed. \u201cBut the King is good, Mother. If something bad happened, it wasn\u2019t the King. It must have been some residual energy from the conquered realm. Father just needs time.\u201d That was the answer he clung to. I couldn\u2019t bring myself to challenge it. What would I say? That the King, the very anchor of our existence, had done this intentionally? I didn\u2019t know that myself\u2014not yet. So I let it fester.\n\nAnd I set about trying to cure him.\n\nOh, the attempts. They are a catalogue of failures so grotesque that recounting them feels like picking at a wound. But you need to understand the depths I went to, so that the final moment\u2014the cure\u2014carries its full weight of absurdity and dread.\n\nThe first real attempt beyond the psycho-surgeon was with a device called the Orphic Engine. A traveling vendor from the fringe systems brought it to our town; he claimed it could extract and crystallize traumatic memories, turning them into physical objects that could be shattered. I paid him everything I had saved from five years of Rogr\u2019s trade. The Engine looked like a glass sphere filled with swirling mercury. When we placed Rogr\u2019s head inside, the mercury coalesced into a shape\u2014a tiny, perfect replica of a throne room. The vendor grinned and activated the extraction. There was a sound like ripping canvas. Then the sphere exploded. The mercury turned into a spray of needles that flayed the vendor\u2019s face off before he could even scream. His body, still standing, jittered as his muscles dissolved, and within seconds he was a puddle of steaming fluid on my floor. The Engine was gone, and Rogr was untouched, still catatonic, though a new trickle of blood ran from his nose.\n\nI cleaned the mess myself. I told Pete it was a burst pipe.\n\nA year later, I heard of a monastery in the Cindered Mountains where the monks had spent centuries developing a mantra that could \u201cpacify the wildest storm of the mind.\u201d I undertook a pilgrimage, leaving Rogr with my sister. The journey was brutal\u2014frozen passes, ravenous montane predators\u2014but I made it. The Abbott, a man so weathered he looked like living bark, agreed to return with me. We brought him to our home. He began the chant, a low drone that seemed to vibrate in my chest. Rogr, for the first time, actually looked at the source of the noise, and I allowed myself a flicker of hope. Then the Abbott\u2019s voice cracked. He coughed, and a mist of blood sprayed from his lips. He tried to continue, but his tongue split open as if sliced by an invisible blade. I watched his larynx collapse inward, his neck caving like a stomped fruit. He died gurgling at my feet, and Rogr simply closed his eyes and retreated back into his corner.\n\nDesperation breeds dark paths. I sought out the remnants of an old order that had once worshipped a being called the Silence Between Stars\u2014a dead god, supposedly, from before Godric\u2019s expansion. They practiced a ritual of \u201csoul-scraping.\u201d Their leader, a woman with hollow eye sockets who called herself the Last Listener, agreed to perform it in exchange for my wedding ring, which had a diamond from the asteroid mines of our homeworld. She took Rogr into a basement and began her work. I was not allowed to watch, but I heard the chanting, and then I heard her scream. When I broke down the door, she was on her knees, her empty sockets now weeping black sludge, and she was laughing\u2014a high, terrible, broken laugh. \u201cHe is marked by the Unconquered Light,\u201d she said. \u201cThere is no scraping that. It is on the other side of his eyes, and it watches me, oh, it watches me still.\u201d She never stopped laughing until she died of a stroke three days later.\n\nThese are just a sample. There were herbalists whose potions reversed their effects and poisoned the brewers; there was an Awakened telepath who tried to build a fortress in Rogr\u2019s mind and instead had his own memories overwritten with fragments of that unseen terror, leaving him a drooling husk. Every single path led to ruin. And through it all, I felt the cold, creeping certainty that I was up against something that did not allow being fixed. It was as if the universe itself forbade anyone from mending what had been shattered in that throne room.\n\nMy despair became a physical thing. I lost weight; my hair grayed in streaks. I would sit beside Rogr at night, listening to his ragged breathing, and I would speak to him\u2014not expecting an answer, just to remind him I was there. I told him about our early years, about the time we first met at the Equinox Festival, about our dreams of opening a larger shop. Sometimes a tear would slide down his cheek, but he never spoke.\n\nThrough it all, I loved him. I never stopped. And he, in his way, never stopped loving me. I could feel it in the rare moments when he would press his forehead to mine, a silent communion more profound than any words.\n\nThen, in the tenth year, the Court Wizard knocked on my door.\n\nThe man called Blake was not what I expected. I had seen the wizards of the realm in broadcasts\u2014stately figures in robes of office, dispensing justice and magic in equal measure. This man had a kind, tired face, a muttonchop beard that needed trimming, and the slumped shoulders of someone carrying a heavy burden. He removed his shoes at the threshold, a common merchant\u2019s custom, which surprised me.\n\n\u201cMy name is Blake,\u201d he said, his voice hoarse. \u201cI\u2019m the King\u2019s friend. And I\u2019m here because I did something very, very stupid ten years ago, and your husband paid the price.\u201d\n\nI listened. He told me about the prank. He told me that Godric, in his infinite power and simplicity, had aimed a microscopic fraction of displeasure at the delegation to play up the \u201ccruel tyrant\u201d persona. He told me that the King had held back so much power that to him, it felt like a gentle exhale. And he told me that the King, knowing everything, had chosen to let Rogr\u2019s suffering run its course because he genuinely believed mortal grit would prevail.\n\n\u201cHe didn\u2019t see it as suffering, exactly,\u201d Blake said, his voice tinged with a frustration that was very, very old. \u201cTo him, it was a\u2026 challenge. A trial that would make Rogr stronger. He sees resilience as a form of beauty. He was, once, a mortal, and he remembers that. He thought he was honoring Rogr by not intervening.\u201d\n\nI felt a scream build in my throat. Ten years of hell, a trial? I wanted to rage. I wanted to strike this wizard, this jester who had planted the idea. But I saw the pain in his eyes, the genuine remorse, and I realized that he, too, was trapped in the wake of a power so immense that his well-meaning joke had become a catastrophe.\n\n\u201cWhy now?\u201d I managed.\n\n\u201cBecause I only found out,\u201d Blake said. \u201cGodric mentioned it in passing\u2014\u2018That delegate from Halden\u2019s Reach, the one who still hasn\u2019t bounced back.\u2019 He said it as if remarking on a stubborn cold. I lost my temper. I yelled at the King of the Omniverse. And he\u2026 listened. He doesn\u2019t always understand, but he listens to me. He agreed to fix it if you would permit.\u201d\n\nMy legs gave out. I slumped into a chair, the weight of ten years crashing down. Pete, who had been standing in the hallway, his eyes wide as saucers, stepped forward. \u201cPlease,\u201d he said to Blake, his voice cracking, \u201cplease. I want my father back.\u201d That simple plea undid something in me.\n\nI took Blake\u2019s hand\u2014the hand of a court wizard, rough with calluses from some honest work\u2014and led him to the bedroom.\n\nRogr was in his usual position by the window. The evening light traced the lines on his face. I knelt before him. \u201cThe man who hurt you can heal you,\u201d I said, keeping my voice steady. \u201cWill you let him?\u201d\n\nRogr\u2019s gaze, which had been a thousand miles away, slowly focused. He looked at Blake. Then at me. His lips parted. \u201cI saw\u2026 a face in the light,\u201d he whispered, and it was the most he had spoken in a year. \u201cIt was only there for a heartbeat. But it knew everything. It could unmake me with a blink. I have been\u2026 unraveling ever since.\u201d He shuddered. \u201cIf that face can undo it\u2026 yes. Yes, I want to be me again.\u201d\n\nThe three of us\u2014Rogr, Pete, and I\u2014stood together in the parlor. Blake asked us to state our consent aloud. We did. And then, instantly, without a sound, a shift.\n\nIt began as a warmth that was not warmth, a pressure that was not pressure. It felt as though the entire house had been submerged in a fathomless ocean and then lifted out again in the space of a heartbeat. Every atom in my body seemed to recognize a presence that was simultaneously infinitely far away and standing right beside me. I could not see him yet, but I knew\u2014with the certainty of a rabbit that senses a descending eagle\u2014that the King was here.\n\nAnd then he was there. Just a man. A handsome, strongly built man in a simple tunic, with a salt-and-pepper beard and eyes that held the light of a billion stars. He didn\u2019t materialize in a flash of glory. He was simply *there*, as if he had been there all along and I had only just been allowed to perceive him.\n\n\u201cRogr of Halden\u2019s Reach,\u201d Godric said, his voice a low, resonant thrum that seemed to bypass my ears and speak directly to my spine. \u201cI owe you an apology. My friend tells me I am an idiot. He is often right.\u201d\n\nThere was no divine thunder, no holy radiance. Just a man, admitting fault. And yet, I could not breathe. My own heart staggered in my chest, because even in this gentle mode, I could feel the edges of what he was holding back. The air was saturated with a silent, crushing potential, like standing at the base of a dam that held back not water, but an entire universe of annihilation.\n\nHe didn\u2019t gesture. He didn\u2019t move. He simply looked at Rogr. A single, quiet look.\n\nRogr\u2019s posture changed. It wasn\u2019t dramatic; it was the subtlest realignment of spine and shoulders, the way a plant turns toward the sun. The gray cast of his skin flushed with healthy color. His eyes cleared, the permanent film of terror lifting like fog burning off a morning meadow. He inhaled, a deep, unlabored breath, and when he exhaled, it was with a sound of relief so profound that tears poured down my face before I even knew I was crying.\n\n\u201cI\u2019m\u2026 hungry,\u201d Rogr said, and his voice was steady and warm. He blinked, looking around the room as if seeing it for the first time. \u201cRosa, I\u2019m ravenous. And my back doesn\u2019t hurt. Why doesn\u2019t my back hurt?\u201d He laughed\u2014a free, startled laugh.\n\nHe looked healthier than I had ever seen him, even before the ceremony. The fine lines on his face had smoothed; his hair, which had been thinning, seemed thicker. He stood straighter, his muscles redefined as if he had spent a year in training. He was, in that moment, the very picture of vitality.\n\nAnd I was shattered. Not by despair, but by the sheer, terrifying ease of it. I fell to my knees\u2014not in worship, though that was part of it, but because my body didn\u2019t know what else to do with the overwhelming cognitive storm. All my efforts, all the blood and screaming and death that had followed my attempts to heal him, had been as effective as ants trying to dam a river. And this being did it without lifting a finger. The gap was not a gap; it was an abyss that had no bottom, a disparity so vast that my mind recoiled from it like a snail from salt.\n\nYet I couldn\u2019t hate him. There, standing in my parlor, was the man who had given my husband back to me. He had done it with a kindness that felt genuine. My heart swelled with a love so fierce it was nauseating. I loved him. I loved my King. And I was, in that same breath, utterly terrified of him.\n\nGodric turned to me and spoke. \u201cRosa. Your devotion is a rare and precious thing. I would like to offer you compensation for the years of trouble. Name anything. A private continent on a world untouched by strife. Dominion over a nascent universe where you may craft your own laws. A million years of your family\u2019s prosperity. Whatever you wish, it is yours.\u201d\n\nThe words hung in the air, each one a universe of impossible wealth. I saw Pete\u2019s jaw drop. I saw Rogr\u2019s eyes widen. But me, I just shook my head. My voice, when it came, was a ruin. \u201cYour Majesty, I have my husband. That is all I ever wanted.\u201d\n\nHe smiled, and there was a flicker of something in his gaze\u2014not pity, but recognition. \u201cYou remind me of someone I knew, a long time ago. Strong, and proud in the best way. Very well.\u201d He gave a slight nod. \u201cYou have my thanks for letting me make this right.\u201d\n\nHe placed a hand on Blake\u2019s shoulder, and they turned to leave. The house seemed to exhale as they moved toward the door. I followed, because I needed to see them go, to confirm that this divine visitation was truly over.\n\nThey descended the front steps, and the evening air was sweet with the scent of jasmine from the neighbor\u2019s garden. I stood in the doorway, my arms wrapped around myself, listening to the rhythmic crunch of their boots on the gravel path.\n\nThen Godric\u2019s voice floated back, casual and warm. \u201cThat went rather well, didn\u2019t it? Got me thinking\u2014we haven\u2019t done a good prank in ages. Next delegation, I could pretend to be a mad jester. Make the walls weep candy. Just for a second, of course. What do you say, Blake?\u201d\n\nBlake\u2019s reply was a strangled, desperate hiss. \u201cI say that I will personally lock you in your chambers if you so much as *think* about another prank. Do you understand me? No. More. Pranks.\u201d\n\nGodric chuckled, a sound so ordinary, so *human*, that it was almost impossible to reconcile with the abyss I knew he contained. \u201cToo late, my friend. You planted the seed. It\u2019s a tradition now.\u201d\n\n\u201cI will salt the earth,\u201d Blake said darkly.\n\nTheir voices faded into the twilight. I remained in the doorway for a long time, the cool air on my face, that conversation replaying in my skull. He was already planning the next one. The King of the Omniverse, the absolute apex of power, was joking about toying with another delegation the way a child jokes about pulling a prank on a sibling. And Blake, his best friend, would protest, and maybe he\u2019d listen, and maybe he wouldn\u2019t. The casualness of it, the sheer nonchalance with which he regarded the souls he could crush, was a horror all its own.\n\nBut I loved him. I loved him for what he had done. I loved him for the smile on Rogr\u2019s face. I loved him for the paradise he maintained.\n\nI went back inside. Rogr was in the kitchen, pulling out bread and cheese, laughing with Pete, who was already planning to apply for the King\u2019s administrative corps. I joined them, and I laughed, and I meant it.\n\nLater, in the deep hours of the night, I lay awake. Rogr slept soundly beside me, his breath deep and even. I traced the line of his shoulder with my fingertips, marveling at its solidity. I thought of the psychics who had died, the monks who had died, the cultists who had died, all because they had dared to touch a wound made by a god\u2019s idle frown. I thought of the casual, unimaginable ease with which that wound had been erased.\n\nAnd I realized that the existential dread would never fully leave me. It had rooted in my marrow, a permanent companion. Because I knew now, with a certainty that went beyond logic, that everything I was, everything I loved, everything that existed, was held in the hand of a being who saw our entire reality as a\u2026 playground. A beloved playground, perhaps, but a playground nonetheless. And that hand could close at any moment, not out of malice, but out of a passing thought.\n\nYet, as I nestled into my husband\u2019s warmth, I found that I could accept that. The dread was the price of the gift. I would pay it willingly, every day, for the rest of my life. Because the alternative was to live without the King\u2019s protection, to be one of the universes that refused mercy and was crushed in an afternoon.\n\nThe King was good. The King was terrifying. Both things were true at once, and that contradiction was the foundation upon which our entire world was built.\n\nI closed my eyes, and when I dreamed, I dreamed of the face in the light\u2014not as Rogr had seen it, in anger, but as I had seen it in my hallway: warm, and kind, and dropping with the infinite weight of a god who thought a \u201clittle prank\u201d was just good fun.\n\nAnd in the dream, I knelt, and I gave thanks, and I did not flinch. Because to flinch would be to admit that the dread had won. And I, Rosa of Halden\u2019s Reach, had survived a decade of hell. I was stronger than my fear.\n\nAt least, that\u2019s what I told myself.\n\n---\n\nNow, this draft is around 2700 words. Let's check. I'll count quickly. (Actually, I'll approximate: about 2700). We'll include that in Blake's explanation, which we did.\n\nNow, let's do a final pass for language and add a bit more meat.\n\nI'll rewrite the whole story but integrate the previous draft and add expansions.\n\n**Final Story (prose paragraphs, 1st POV Rosa):**\n\n[I'll write as a single block of text with paragraphs, no headings.]\n\nLet's craft:\n\n---\n\nI remember the afternoon Rogr came back from the Ceremony of Nine Banners, the day the light in him went out. He had been chosen as one of three hundred provincial delegates\u2014a minor honor, really, a way for the Crown to include common folk in the pageantry of conquest. He was to stand in the Throne Room of the Resplendent Spire and present a bolt of our district\u2019s finest weave as a token of fealty. He practiced his bow for a week, and he was glowing with pride when he left. He returned on foot, with no escort, his tunic untucked and soaked in a cold, metallic sweat that smelled like the air after a lightning strike. His eyes were so wide the whites showed all around the iris, and his pupils were the size of black moons. When I touched his arm, he blinked and then his face collapsed into an expression of such raw, infantile terror that I stumbled backward and nearly fell over the hall rug.\n\n\u201cRogr?\u201d I said.\n\nHe opened his mouth, but no words came. Just a croak that spiraled into a high, keening whimper. He walked past me in a shuffle, found the corner of our bedroom where two walls met, and he wedged himself into that angle. He pulled a chair in front of him like a barricade, and for three days he did not move except to take small sips of water when I pressed the cup to his lips. At night, he screamed. Not words\u2014a sound that started in the base of his spine and ripped upward, pure horror given voice, shattering the stillness of our house. I held him, or tried to, but his body was rigid, and the few times his eyes met mine there was no recognition. Only a deep, abiding terror that seemed to gaze at something behind my face.\n\nOur son Pete was seven. He stood in the doorway that first week, his small fists clenched, and he asked me why Papa was crying. I told him Papa had a very bad dream that wouldn\u2019t let go. It was the best I could do. How could I explain that the father who had once built him a treehouse and taught him to whistle through a blade of grass had been hollowed out by an afternoon in the presence of our beloved King? I didn\u2019t understand it myself, not yet. I only knew that something unspeakable had happened in that throne room, and whatever it was, it had stopped Rogr\u2019s mind the way a boot stops an ant.\n\nThe first months, I believed he would recover. He was an Awakened man\u2014strong, resilient, his endurance and wisdom increasing each day past twenty as the King\u2019s gift promised. Surely such a man could fight off a mere trauma. But the Awakening did nothing for this. It was as if the wound existed on a different axis, one that his multiplied strength could not touch.\n\nI sought help. The first was a renowned psycho-surgeon from the capital, a woman named Dr. Elara who had allegedly cured entire regiments of combat fatigue. She laid her palms on Rogr\u2019s temples and began a standard memory-smoothing protocol. The moment her consciousness brushed the edge of whatever black knot sat in his mind, she shrieked and fell backward, blood jetting from her nostrils in a fan that painted the wall. She died three days later of a total neurological cascade\u2014all her nerves firing simultaneously until her body simply cooked from within her skin. The coroner\u2019s report said \u201cunexplained resonance.\u201d\n\nI did not stop. I could not. I found a traveling vendor with a device called the Orphic Engine, a sphere of swirling mercury that could supposedly extract traumatic memories and crystallize them into physical objects to be shattered. I paid him everything I had saved from five years of Rogr\u2019s textile trade. When we placed Rogr\u2019s head inside the sphere, the mercury coalesced into a shape\u2014a tiny, perfect replica of a great hall, with a speck at its center that I knew, without being told, was the King. The vendor grinned and activated the extraction. There was a sound like ripping canvas. The sphere exploded, and the mercury turned into a spray of needles that flayed the vendor\u2019s face off while he was still standing. His body jittered as his muscles dissolved, and within seconds he was a puddle of steaming fluid on my floor. The Engine was gone. Rogr was untouched, though a new trickle of blood ran from his nose.\n\nI cleaned the mess with a bucket and a scrub brush. I told Pete a pipe had burst.\n\nI heard of a monastery in the Cindered Mountains where monks had spent centuries perfecting a mantra that could pacify the wildest storms of the mind. I undertook a pilgrimage, leaving Rogr with my sister. I crossed frozen passes where the wind cut to the bone, and I climbed cliffs that a woman my age had no business climbing. The Abbott, a man so weathered he looked like living bark, agreed to return with me. In our humble parlor, he began the chant. The low drone vibrated in my chest, and I saw Rogr\u2019s eyes focus for the first time in months. A single tear rolled down his cheek. The hope was so sharp it hurt. Then the Abbott\u2019s voice cracked. He coughed, and a pink mist sprayed from his lips. He tried to continue, but his tongue split open as if sliced by an invisible razor. I watched, frozen, as his larynx collapsed inward, his neck caving like a stomped fruit. He died gurgling at my feet. And Rogr simply closed his eyes and retreated back into himself.\n\nDesperation grew teeth. I sought the remnants of an old order that had once worshipped a being called the Silence Between Stars. They practiced a forbidden ritual of \u201csoul-scraping.\u201d Their leader, a woman with hollow, scarred eye sockets who called herself the Last Listener, agreed to perform it in exchange for my wedding ring\u2014the diamond from the asteroid mines of my homeworld. She took Rogr into a basement and began her work. I was not allowed to watch, but I heard the chant rise to a frenzy, and then I heard her scream. When I broke down the door, she was on her knees, her empty sockets now weeping black, viscous sludge, and she was laughing\u2014a high, shattered, broken laugh that raised the hairs on my arms. \u201cHe is marked by the Unconquered Light,\u201d she rasped. \u201cThere is no scraping that. It is on the other side of his eyes, and it watches me still, oh, it watches me.\u201d She laughed until she died of a stroke three days later.\n\nThere were other attempts. An Awakened sage who tried to weave a mental shield around Rogr; the shield inverted and fed the sage\u2019s own terrors into his brain until he clawed out his left eye. A back-alley enchanter who brewed an elixir of calm; when Rogr inhaled the steam, the liquid turned to acid and ate through the table and the floor, releasing fumes that drove the enchanter mad, and he ran into the street and was never seen again. Every single path led to ruin\u2014ruin for the healers, while Rogr remained perfectly, horribly intact. It was as if the universe itself had decreed that nothing was permitted to touch what the King had, in a single fraction of a moment, inscribed on my husband\u2019s soul.\n\nThrough it all, Pete grew. He was a good boy, with his father\u2019s quick smile and my stubbornness. He idolized the King, as all children did. Our home had a small printed portrait of Godric in the kitchen, and every morning before school, Pete would pause before it and give a little salute. \u201cFor the glory of Thronegate,\u201d he\u2019d say, and I would ruffle his hair and try not to look at Rogr\u2019s white-knuckled hands. Pete did not understand why his father flinched at the name of the King. He would come home from his lessons, full of stories about the latest glorious conquest\u2014how a universe had been offered mercy and had refused, and how a squad of five Thronegate men had, in less than thirty minutes, ended a civilization that had prepared for five years. The pride in his voice made Rogr shake so badly that he would have to leave the room. I tried to explain to Pete once, when he was fifteen, that his father\u2019s illness was connected to an experience with the King\u2019s presence. Pete\u2019s brow had furrowed. \u201cBut the King is good, Mother. If Father was hurt, the King didn\u2019t mean to. Maybe it\u2019s a test? A trial to make him stronger?\u201d I had no answer. His faith was a wall I could not break.\n\nI loved Rogr. I loved him with a ferocity that defied the decade of silent dinners and screaming nights. And he loved me. In his rare lucid moments, he would press his forehead to mine and whisper my name, and in those syllables I heard the echo of the man who had once danced with me at the Equinox Festival, laughing in the rain. Those moments were water in a desert; I lived for them.\n\nAnd then, in the tenth year, I opened my door to a stranger with a friendly muttonchop beard and the weight of a galaxy in his eyes.\n\nHe introduced himself as Blake, Court Wizard to King Godric. My first instinct was to drop to one knee, but he held up a hand with a tired, almost pained smile. \u201cPlease, don\u2019t. I\u2019m just a man. And I\u2019ve come to apologize.\u201d\n\nI let him in because his face was honest, and because I was too exhausted to do anything else. He stood in my hallway, removing his shoes out of a merchant\u2019s habit, and he told me a story. He spoke of a king who, long ago, had been a mortal man, a father, a friend. He spoke of the King\u2019s trust in him, and how, as a joke, he had once suggested that Godric could play up the \u201ccruel tyrant\u201d persona for a new group of delegates, just for a few seconds, to see their faces before revealing his true, kind nature. Godric, loving the idea as a prank among friends, had agreed.\n\n\u201cI thought it would be funny,\u201d Blake said, his voice cracking. \u201cYou have to understand, Godric\u2026 he\u2019s not cruel by nature. But he\u2019s been alone in power for so long. He thought he was holding back everything\u2014literally ninety-nine point a billion decimals of his true presence. To him, what he projected was a faint shadow of a frown, barely a whisper. He genuinely believed the delegates would laugh it off after he revealed the joke. But I didn\u2019t realize\u2014he didn\u2019t realize\u2014that even that infinitesimal sliver, that fraction so small it\u2019s practically zero, is still an existential avalanche for a mortal mind. The omniverse bends to his slightest will; it cannot help but do so. Your husband was one of those delegates. He was exposed to that fraction for a fraction of a second.\u201d\n\nMy throat closed. \u201cTen years,\u201d I said. \u201cTen years of hell, because of a prank?\u201d\n\nBlake\u2019s eyes were red. \u201cI only found out a few days ago. Godric mentioned it casually. \u2018That delegate from Halden\u2019s Reach who still hasn\u2019t bounced back\u2014remarkable, the variation in mortal resilience.\u2019 He said it while moving a chess piece. He knew everything, of course. He always knows. But he had convinced himself that your husband would overcome it. He respects grit, you see. He was once a mortal himself. He thought he was honoring Rogr by not interfering. He thought time would heal.\u201d\n\nThe anger that surged through me then was a living creature. I wanted to claw at the walls. But I looked at Blake, and I saw that he was already clawing at his own insides. So I swallowed the fire and said, \u201cWhat can be done?\u201d\n\n\u201cI yelled at him,\u201d Blake said. \u201cI told him he was a universe-damned fool. And he listened. He said he would fix it, but only if you and Rogr consent. He\u2019s not a monster; he just\u2026 forgets the scale of the gap. Will you allow me to call him?\u201d\n\nI took Blake to the bedroom. Rogr was in his chair, staring at the sunset. I knelt and took his hands. \u201cThe man who cursed you can heal you,\u201d I said. \u201cDo you want that?\u201d\n\nFor the first time in months, Rogr\u2019s gaze found mine and stayed. His voice was a whisper of dry leaves. \u201cI saw a face in the light. It was only there for a heartbeat. But it knew everything. It could unmake me with a blink. I have been\u2026 dying that blink\u2026 for ten years.\u201d He took a shuddering breath. \u201cIf that face will undo it\u2026 yes. I want to be me again.\u201d\n\nPete, who had been standing at the doorway with tears streaming down his cheeks, stepped forward. \u201cFather, please. The King can fix anything. He is mercy itself.\u201d There was such desperate faith in his voice that it broke my heart a little more.\n\nWe gathered in the parlor. Blake asked us to state our consent aloud, and we did\u2014Rogr, Pete, and I, three voices in the quiet room.\n\nAnd then the room changed.\n\nIt was not a sound or a light. It was a shift in the fundamental texture of existence. A presence that was not a presence descended, like an ocean settling over the entire house without weight. The air became thick and watchful, and every atom in my body revolted and rejoiced at the same time. I felt an urge to prostrate myself, not from fear, but from a recognition so deep it was cellular: a predator had entered the space, a predator so far above the food chain that the concept of \u201cchain\u201d lost all meaning. And yet, there was no hostility. Only a calm, gentle attention that was somehow more terrifying than any rage.\n\nBetween one heartbeat and the next, he was there. King Godric, of Olympus-Secundus, ruler of the omniverse, stood in my parlor.\n\nHe was a tall, muscular man, aged somewhere around forty-five by appearance, though I knew he was over ten thousand years old. His hair was short, his beard neatly trimmed and flecked with salt and pepper, his face handsome and utterly unremarkable save for the eyes\u2014eyes that held the light of a billion dead stars and a warmth that was, against all logic, genuine. He wore simple clothes, a dark blue tunic and worn boots. He looked like a kindly father, not the absolute apex of all things. And when he spoke, his voice was a low, rich thrum that seemed to bypass my ears and vibrate directly in my bones.\n\n\u201cRogr of Halden\u2019s Reach,\u201d he said. \u201cI owe you an apology. My friend tells me I am an idiot. He is often right.\u201d\n\nHe did not gesture. He did not move. He simply looked at Rogr.\n\nWhat happened next I cannot fully describe, because it involved no visible change and yet was the most profound transformation I have ever witnessed. Rogr\u2019s posture, which had been a permanent cringe, eased. Color flooded his cheeks\u2014a healthy, vibrant flush that I hadn\u2019t seen since before the ceremony. His eyes, which had been glassy and unfocused, cleared into a sharp, warm brown. The lines of tension around his mouth vanished. He took a breath\u2014a deep, full, unlabored breath\u2014and then he laughed. A short, startled laugh that rose into a rolling, joyful sound.\n\n\u201cI\u2019m\u2026 I\u2019m hungry, Rosa,\u201d he said, and his voice was steady and clear and so full of life that I burst into sobs. \u201cI\u2019m starving. And my back\u2014why doesn\u2019t my back ache? I feel like I could lift the house.\u201d\n\nHe looked healthier than I had ever seen him. His hair, which had been thinning and dull, now seemed thicker and lustrous. His skin had a glow that wasn\u2019t just the absence of pallor but a positive radiance. He was the picture of health, as if he had never spent a decade in a living nightmare\u2014as if he had been dipped in a fountain of pure vitality. Pete rushed into his arms, and Rogr caught him and spun him around with an ease that spoke of muscles newly remade.\n\nI fell to my knees. I wasn\u2019t praying; my body just couldn\u2019t hold up under the cognitive weight. In the span of a single glance, the thing that had consumed my life for ten years, the thing that had killed so many in my desperate attempts to cure it, had been erased. Not treated. Not healed in the slow, painful way of medicine. Erased. As if it had never been. And the being who had done it was already looking at me with a gentle, faintly sorrowful smile, as if he were a neighbor who had accidentally broken a fence post and was sorry for the inconvenience.\n\nThe terror of that ease, that bottomless, effortless power, crawled into my chest and made a nest there, right beside the overwhelming gratitude and love I felt. I loved him. I loved my King for giving me my husband back. And I was, in the same marrow, horrified by him.\n\nGodric turned to me. \u201cRosa. Your devotion is a rare and precious thing. I would like to offer you compensation for the trouble. Name anything you desire. A private continent on a paradise world, untouched by strife. Dominion over a nascent universe where you and your family may craft your own laws and live in eternal peace. A hundred thousand years of prosperity for your bloodline. Whatever you wish, it is yours.\u201d\n\nThe words hung in the air like a shower of diamonds. Any one of those things would have elevated us beyond the wildest dreams of anyone in the galaxy. And the chilling thing was that I knew, in my bones, that he meant it. These treasures were nothing to him. A continent, a universe\u2014they were trinkets, a few spare coins tossed to a beggar. I could have asked for a throne of stars and he would have granted it with the same warmth.\n\nBut I shook my head. My voice was thick. \u201cYour Majesty, I have my husband. That is all I ever wanted. I need nothing more.\u201d\n\nHe nodded, and there was no surprise in his expression. A flicker of something\u2014respect, perhaps\u2014crossed his features. \u201cYou remind me of someone I knew, a long time ago. Strong, and proud in the best way. Very well. You have my thanks for allowing me to make this right.\u201d\n\nHe placed a hand on Blake\u2019s shoulder, and they turned to leave. I followed them to the door because it felt wrong not to. The evening outside was soft and gold, and my legs still felt like water. They descended the front steps, and I lingered in the doorway, my hand on the jamb.\n\nThen I heard Godric\u2019s voice, casual and warm, drifting back on the breeze. \u201cYou know, Blake, that went rather well. It\u2019s given me an idea. Next delegation, perhaps I should try a different act\u2014maybe a mad jester. I could make the walls weep candy for a moment. Just a second. See their faces.\u201d\n\nBlake\u2019s reply was a strangled, panicked rasp. \u201cI will personally find a way to chain you to your throne if you even *whisper* the word \u2018prank\u2019 again. Do you understand me? No. More. Pranks.\u201d\n\nGodric chuckled, a sound so ordinary and amiable that it was almost impossible to reconcile with the abyss I knew he contained. \u201cToo late, my friend. You planted the seed. It\u2019s tradition now.\u201d\n\n\u201cI will salt the earth,\u201d Blake said darkly, \u201cand then I will cry. No more.\u201d\n\nThey walked on, their voices blending into the twilight. I stood frozen, the echo of that exchange rattling around my skull like a loose gear. He was planning another one. The King of the Omniverse, the being whose merest thought could unmake all of creation, was joking about toying with the minds of innocents for the amusement of his best friend, and his best friend was saying no with the exasperation of a man who had seen this too many times.\n\nI went inside. Rogr was in the kitchen, making a massive sandwich and laughing at Pete\u2019s jokes. They were planning to go to the town square the next day to listen to the crier announce the latest off-world news. Pete wanted to apply to the King\u2019s administrative corps. Rogr was already talking about reopening the textile shop. The house was full of light and noise and life, all because the King had decided, in a single instant, that my husband should be healthy.\n\nI joined them. I laughed when they laughed. I let Rogr pull me into a fierce embrace, and I breathed in the scent of him\u2014alive, whole, happy. I loved the King. I revered him. I would light a candle at the temple and bow my head and give thanks with a full heart.\n\nBut late that night, when the house was still and Rogr\u2019s deep, peaceful breathing filled the room, I lay awake. The existential dread had not left. It had burrowed into my marrow, a permanent tenant. Because I knew now, with a certainty that transcended logic, that everything I loved\u2014Rogr, Pete, this house, this world\u2014was held in the palm of a hand that could close at any moment, not out of malice, but out of a passing whim, a joke, a \u201cprank\u201d meant for a friend. The distance between us and our King was not a gap; it was an abyss that had no bottom. And the only thing that kept us safe was his genuine, sincere kindness.\n\nThat kindness was real. I had felt it in my own parlor. He was good. He was terrifying. Both things were true at once, and that contradiction was the bedrock on which our entire civilization was built. I had to hold it in my mind without shattering, and I found that I could. Because the alternative\u2014a universe without his protection, one of those worlds that refused mercy and was erased in an afternoon\u2014was far worse.\n\nThe dread was a price I would pay willingly. I would pay it every day for the rest of my life.\n\nI nestled into my husband\u2019s warmth, and I closed my eyes. In my dreams, I saw the face in the light, and it smiled at me, and I smiled back without flinching.\n\n---\n\n**Word count check:** This is about 3100 words. Right in the range. Pete did not understand why his father flinched at the name of the King. He would come home from his lessons, full of stories about the latest glorious conquest\u2014how a universe had been offered mercy and had refused, and how a squad of five Thronegate men had, in less than thirty minutes, ended a civilization that had prepared for five years. The pride in his voice made Rogr shake so badly that he would have to leave the room. I tried to explain to Pete once, when he was fifteen, that his father\u2019s illness was connected to an experience with the King\u2019s presence. Pete\u2019s brow had furrowed. \u201cBut the King is good, Mother. If Father was hurt, the King didn\u2019t mean to. Maybe it\u2019s a test? A trial to make him stronger?\u201d I had no answer. His faith was a wall I could not break.\n\nI loved Rogr. I loved him with a ferocity that defied the decade of silent dinners and screaming nights. And he loved me. In his rare lucid moments, he would press his forehead to mine and whisper my name, and in those syllables I heard the echo of the man who had once danced with me at the Equinox Festival, laughing in the rain. Those moments were water in a desert; I lived for them.\n\nAnd then, in the tenth year, I opened my door to a stranger with a friendly muttonchop beard and the weight of a galaxy in his eyes.\n\nHe introduced himself as Blake, Court Wizard to King Godric. My first instinct was to drop to one knee, but he held up a hand with a tired, almost pained smile. \u201cPlease, don\u2019t. I\u2019m just a man. And I\u2019ve come to apologize.\u201d\n\nI let him in because his face was honest, and because I was too exhausted to do anything else. He stood in my hallway, removing his shoes out of a merchant\u2019s habit, and he told me a story. He spoke of a king who, long ago, had been a mortal man, a father, a friend. He spoke of the King\u2019s trust in him, and how, as a joke, he had once suggested that Godric could play up the \u201ccruel tyrant\u201d persona for a new group of delegates, just for a few seconds, to see their faces before revealing his true, kind nature. Godric, loving the idea as a prank among friends, had agreed.\n\n\u201cI thought it would be funny,\u201d Blake said, his voice cracking. \u201cYou have to understand, Godric\u2026 he\u2019s not cruel by nature. But he\u2019s been alone in power for so long. He thought he was holding back everything\u2014literally ninety\u2011nine point a billion decimals of his true presence. To him, what he projected was a faint shadow of a frown, barely a whisper. He genuinely believed the delegates would laugh it off after he revealed the joke. But I didn\u2019t realize\u2014he didn\u2019t realize\u2014that even that infinitesimal sliver, that fraction so small it\u2019s practically zero, is still an existential avalanche for a mortal mind. The omniverse bends to his slightest will; it cannot help but do so. Your husband was one of those delegates. He was exposed to that fraction for a fraction of a second.\u201d\n\nMy throat closed. \u201cTen years,\u201d I said. \u201cTen years of hell, because of a prank?\u201d\n\nBlake\u2019s eyes were red. \u201cI only found out a few days ago. Godric mentioned it casually. \u2018That delegate from Halden\u2019s Reach who still hasn\u2019t bounced back\u2014remarkable, the variation in mortal resilience.\u2019 He said it while moving a chess piece. He knew everything, of course. He always knows. But he had convinced himself that your husband would overcome it. He respects grit, you see. He was once a mortal himself. He thought he was honoring Rogr by not interfering. He thought time would heal.\u201d\n\nThe anger that surged through me then was a living creature. I wanted to claw at the walls. But I looked at Blake, and I saw that he was already clawing at his own insides. So I swallowed the fire and said, \u201cWhat can be done?\u201d\n\n\u201cI yelled at him,\u201d Blake said. \u201cI told him he was a universe\u2011damned fool. And he listened. He said he would fix it, but only if you and Rogr consent. He\u2019s not a monster; he just\u2026 forgets the scale of the gap. Will you allow me to call him?\u201d\n\nI took Blake to the bedroom. Rogr was in his chair, staring at the sunset. I knelt and took his hands. \u201cThe man who cursed you can heal you,\u201d I said. \u201cDo you want that?\u201d\n\nFor the first time in months, Rogr\u2019s gaze found mine and stayed. His voice was a whisper of dry leaves. \u201cI saw a face in the light. It was only there for a heartbeat. But it knew everything. It could unmake me with a blink. I have been\u2026 dying that blink\u2026 for ten years.\u201d He took a shuddering breath. \u201cIf that face will undo it\u2026 yes. I want to be me again.\u201d\n\nPete, who had been standing at the doorway with tears streaming down his cheeks, stepped forward. \u201cFather, please. The King can fix anything. He is mercy itself.\u201d There was such desperate faith in his voice that it broke my heart a little more.\n\nWe gathered in the parlor. Blake asked us to state our consent aloud, and we did\u2014Rogr, Pete, and I, three voices in the quiet room.\n\nAnd then the room changed.\n\nIt was not a sound or a light. It was a shift in the fundamental texture of existence. A presence that was not a presence descended, like an ocean settling over the entire house without weight. The air became thick and watchful, and every atom in my body revolted and rejoiced at the same time. I felt an urge to prostrate myself, not from fear, but from a recognition so deep it was cellular: a predator had entered the space, a predator so far above the food chain that the concept of \u201cchain\u201d lost all meaning. And yet, there was no hostility. Only a calm, gentle attention that was somehow more terrifying than any rage.\n\nBetween one heartbeat and the next, he was there. King Godric, of Olympus\u2011Secundus, ruler of the omniverse, stood in my parlor.\n\nHe was a tall, muscular man, aged somewhere around forty\u2011five by appearance, though I knew he was over ten thousand years old. His hair was short, his beard neatly trimmed and flecked with salt and pepper, his face handsome and utterly unremarkable save for the eyes\u2014eyes that held the light of a billion dead stars and a warmth that was, against all logic, genuine. He wore simple clothes, a dark blue tunic and worn boots. He looked like a kindly father, not the absolute apex of all things. And when he spoke, his voice was a low, rich thrum that seemed to bypass my ears and vibrate directly in my bones.\n\n\u201cRogr of Halden\u2019s Reach,\u201d he said. \u201cI owe you an apology. My friend tells me I am an idiot. He is often right.\u201d\n\nHe did not gesture. He did not move. He simply looked at Rogr.\n\nWhat happened next I cannot fully describe, because it involved no visible change and yet was the most profound transformation I have ever witnessed. Rogr\u2019s posture, which had been a permanent cringe, eased. Color flooded his cheeks\u2014a healthy, vibrant flush that I hadn\u2019t seen since before the ceremony. His eyes, which had been glassy and unfocused, cleared into a sharp, warm brown. The lines of tension around his mouth vanished. He took a breath\u2014a deep, full, unlabored breath\u2014and then he laughed. A short, startled laugh that rose into a rolling, joyful sound.\n\n\u201cI\u2019m\u2026 I\u2019m hungry, Rosa,\u201d he said, and his voice was steady and clear and so full of life that I burst into sobs. \u201cI\u2019m starving. And my back\u2014why doesn\u2019t my back ache? I feel like I could lift the house.\u201d\n\nHe looked healthier than I had ever seen him. His hair, which had been thinning and dull, now seemed thicker and lustrous. His skin had a glow that wasn\u2019t just the absence of pallor but a positive radiance. He was the picture of health, as if he had never spent a decade in a living nightmare\u2014as if he had been dipped in a fountain of pure vitality. Pete rushed into his arms, and Rogr caught him and spun him around with an ease that spoke of muscles newly remade.\n\nI fell to my knees. I wasn\u2019t praying; my body just couldn\u2019t hold up under the cognitive weight. In the span of a single glance, the thing that had consumed my life for ten years, the thing that had killed so many in my desperate attempts to cure it, had been erased. Not treated. Not healed in the slow, painful way of medicine. Erased. As if it had never been. And the being who had done it was already looking at me with a gentle, faintly sorrowful smile, as if he were a neighbor who had accidentally broken a fence post and was sorry for the inconvenience.\n\nThe terror of that ease, that bottomless, effortless power, crawled into my chest and made a nest there, right beside the overwhelming gratitude and love I felt. I loved him. I loved my King for giving me my husband back. And I was, in the same marrow, horrified by him.\n\nGodric turned to me. \u201cRosa. Your devotion is a rare and precious thing. I would like to offer you compensation for the trouble. Name anything you desire. A private continent on a paradise world, untouched by strife. Dominion over a nascent universe where you and your family may craft your own laws and live in eternal peace. A hundred thousand years of prosperity for your bloodline. Whatever you wish, it is yours.\u201d\n\nThe words hung in the air like a shower of diamonds. Any one of those things would have elevated us beyond the wildest dreams of anyone in the galaxy. And the chilling thing was that I knew, in my bones, that he meant it. These treasures were nothing to him. A continent, a universe\u2014they were trinkets, a few spare coins tossed to a beggar. I could have asked for a throne of stars and he would have granted it with the same warmth.\n\nBut I shook my head. My voice was thick. \u201cYour Majesty, I have my husband. That is all I ever wanted. I need nothing more.\u201d\n\nHe nodded, and there was no surprise in his expression. A flicker of something\u2014respect, perhaps\u2014crossed his features. \u201cYou remind me of someone I knew, a long time ago. Strong, and proud in the best way. Very well. You have my thanks for allowing me to make this right.\u201d\n\nHe placed a hand on Blake\u2019s shoulder, and they turned to leave. I followed them to the door because it felt wrong not to. The evening outside was soft and gold, and my legs still felt like water. They descended the front steps, and I lingered in the doorway, my hand on the jamb.\n\nThen I heard Godric\u2019s voice, casual and warm, drifting back on the breeze. \u201cYou know, Blake, that went rather well. It\u2019s given me an idea. Next delegation, perhaps I should try a different act\u2014maybe a mad jester. I could make the walls weep candy for a moment. Just a second. See their faces.\u201d\n\nBlake\u2019s reply was a strangled, panicked rasp. \u201cI will personally find a way to chain you to your throne if you even whisper the word \u2018prank\u2019 again. Do you understand me? No. More. Pranks.\u201d\n\nGodric chuckled, a sound so ordinary and amiable that it was almost impossible to reconcile with the abyss I knew he contained. \u201cToo late, my friend. You planted the seed. It\u2019s tradition now.\u201d\n\n\u201cI will salt the earth,\u201d Blake said darkly, \u201cand then I will cry. No more.\u201d\n\nThey walked on, their voices blending into the twilight. I stood frozen, the echo of that exchange rattling around my skull like a loose gear. He was planning another one. The King of the Omniverse, the being whose merest thought could unmake all of creation, was joking about toying with the minds of innocents for the amusement of his best friend, and his best friend was saying no with the exasperation of a man who had seen this too many times.\n\nI went inside. Rogr was in the kitchen, making a massive sandwich and laughing at Pete\u2019s jokes. They were planning to go to the town square the next day to listen to the crier announce the latest off\u2011world news. Pete wanted to apply to the King\u2019s administrative corps. Rogr was already talking about reopening the textile shop. The house was full of light and noise and life, all because the King had decided, in a single instant, that my husband should be healthy.\n\nI joined them. I laughed when they laughed. I let Rogr pull me into a fierce embrace, and I breathed in the scent of him\u2014alive, whole, happy. I loved the King. I revered him. I would light a candle at the temple and bow my head and give thanks with a full heart.\n\nBut late that night, when the house was still and Rogr\u2019s deep, peaceful breathing filled the room, I lay awake. The existential dread had not left. It had burrowed into my marrow, a permanent tenant. Because I knew now, with a certainty that transcended logic, that everything I loved\u2014Rogr, Pete, this house, this world\u2014was held in the palm of a hand that could close at any moment, not out of malice, but out of a passing whim, a joke, a \u201cprank\u201d meant for a friend. The distance between us and our King was not a gap; it was an abyss that had no bottom. And the only thing that kept us safe was his genuine, sincere kindness.\n\nThat kindness was real. I had felt it in my own parlor. He was good. He was terrifying. Both things were true at once, and that contradiction was the bedrock on which our entire civilization was built. I had to hold it in my mind without shattering, and I found that I could. Because the alternative\u2014a universe without his protection, one of those worlds that refused mercy and was erased in an afternoon\u2014was far worse.\n\nThe dread was a price I would pay willingly. I would pay it every day for the rest of my life.\n\nI nestled into my husband\u2019s warmth, and I closed my eyes. In my dreams, I saw the face in the light, and it smiled at me, and I smiled back without flinching."

Tim cracks a joke. But there's underlying dread because Tim knows what Godric is.\n- Godric explains he's curious if his \"Gent\" will feel effort. This is the first time the aura might have to try. Tim thinks about how insane that is.\n- The resistance arrives in full force: number them in the quadrillions, with gods, etc. Show their powers in exaggerated detail. Use some examples: an army of \"Shrike-like\" time-reversing assassins, a fleet of TARDIS-like vessels that can rewrite history, a being like \"The One Above All\" but from another universe, a sword that can kill anything, even concepts. I'll pick 4 specific: 1) A collective of \"Alpha Omegas\" \u2013 beings that transcend all narratives, each can uncreate multiverses with a thought. 2) The \"Singularity Cannon\" \u2013 a weapon that fires a point of absolute zero-existence, deleting anything from past, present, future. 3) \"The Unraveler\" \u2013 an entity woven from paradoxes, immune to all damage, can undo the fabric of reality. 4) The \"Time-Knife\" \u2013 a blade that severs causality, used by a warrior king who has killed countless cosmic entities. The rest: billions of lesser but still OP entities. All of them combined are hyped as unstoppable.\n\n- The battle: Godric hasn't moved, he's having tea or something. Tim watches. The resistance attacks all at once. But they never reach him. The air itself becomes murder. The aura, Gent, engages. Tim describes the sensation: an invisible, oppressive presence, like the universe's own immune system.\n\n- The slaughter: For each of the 4, show in detail how they die grotesquely. E.g., The Alpha Omegas try to erase Godric from existence; instead, their own minds are invaded and they are forced to experience every possible death at once, their bodies splitting into fractals of gore. The Singularity Cannon fires; the beam just stops a mile from Godric, and then the concept of the cannon is retroactively deleted, and its operators are stretched into infinite timelines where they are eternally tortured. All in a fraction of a second. The rest: a simultaneous wave of annihilation, described as a brief cacophony of screams and then silence. The ground is soaked with blood and cosmic residue.\n\n- Tim's horror: his internal monologue. He can't comprehend the ease. He looks at Godric, who is calmly watching, maybe commenting \"I told Gent to hold back, but it seems it didn't listen well enough.\" Godric then speaks to the air, \"Gent, you were supposed to use only a fraction. What part of 99.999...% did you not get?\" And the aura, sentient, communicates something. Tim maybe hears a faint hum, like a puppy whining. Godric sighs. \"I'll have to teach you restraint.\" Tim reflects on how Godric himself accidentally destroys universes. This contrast adds to the dread.\n\n- The amplification realization: Tim is staring at the dissipating energy of the aura, and he thinks about the fact that every Planck second, Godric gets infinitely more powerful. He tries to grasp it: the Godric of a moment ago is infinitely weaker than now. The resistance could have attacked at any point in time, but they chose now, making it the worst possible moment. The math is beyond him, but the sense of futility crushes him.\n\n- The evolution: Suddenly, the aura pulses. Tim feels a new layer unfold. The sky or the fabric of reality shimmers, and for a moment, Tim perceives that the aura now has the power to, say, erase not just the resistance, but the very concept of resistance across all possible realities, should it choose. Or something equally terrifying. Godric notices, and his face lights up with a genuine, warm smile. \"Well, look at that. Gent's learned a new trick.\" He chuckles, proud. Tim describes it as a father watching a puppy take its first steps. The absurdity is overwhelming.\n\n- Tim's cognitive dissonance: Godric turns to Tim, and with that fatherly warmth, asks if he's feeling well, because Tim looks pale. Tim manages a weak smile, says he's fine. The story ends with Tim's internal scream: the nice king who pats him on the back is the same being whose stray heat just obliterated the most powerful coalition ever. And that's just his aura.
