                    "text": "My hands hadn\u2019t stopped shaking in six hours. I\u2019d been standing at the great window of the Observatorium, a crystal blister on the outer hull of Olympus Secundus, for so long my legs had passed through numbness and into a kind of hollow buzzing. The view looked directly down into the Bleached Expanse, a void between universes our King had chosen for the occasion because it was, in his words, \u201cnice and empty, so we won\u2019t have to fix anything later.\u201d I\u2019d laughed at that, a reflexive bark, because when your immortal omnipotent monarch makes a joke, you laugh. Only now, staring at the thing coalescing in the void, the laugh had curdled into something that sat at the back of my throat like wet ash.\n\nGodric lounged in a chair behind me, one leg hooked over the armrest, a cup of something steaming balanced on the flat of his thumb. He hadn\u2019t looked out the window once. \u201cStop gawking, Tim. You\u2019ll exhaust yourself before the entertainment starts.\u201d\n\n\u201cEntertainment,\u201d I repeated. \u201cThat\u2019s what we\u2019re calling the largest military coalition in the history of the omniverse. Fifteen hundred universes. Every banished god, every deposed tyrant, every reality-enduring superweapon that the last twenty thousand years forgot to bury deep enough. And you\u2019re calling it entertainment.\u201d\n\nHe made a soft, thoughtful noise, more breath than voice. \u201cI was going to call it a pet project. But entertainment sounds more hopeful.\u201d The warmth in his tone was sincere. He wasn\u2019t gloating. He was, as far as I could tell, genuinely looking forward to watching his passive aura, a sentient discharge he\u2019d named Gent, finally have to exert itself a little.\n\nThat was the part I couldn\u2019t wrap my mind around. Godric had let this happen. For two and a half millennia, by my count, he\u2019d kept Gent on a leash, deliberately excluding this swelling tide of malcontents from the passive annihilation that automatically snuffed out any other conceivable threat. The reason? Gent had never, in its twenty-thousand-year existence, felt effort. Godric was curious if it could. That was the entire strategic calculus. And the resistance, convinced they\u2019d eluded his omniscience through layers of timeloop obfuscation and dimensional cloaking, had spent every one of those twenty-five centuries unknowingly feeding the Weakness Paradox with every plan they made, every thought they formed about the chinks they imagined in his armor. Their preparations had made him infinitely more invincible than he\u2019d been when they started, and they had no idea.\n\nI\u2019d tried, once, to explain this to a visiting dignitary from a subjugated universe who\u2019d asked, with trembling politeness, if Godric had any weaknesses. I\u2019d managed the first syllable of \u201cno\u201d and then my throat had closed up because the full scope of what \u201cno\u201d meant was a black ocean with no bottom, and I didn\u2019t want to look at it.\n\nNow I was looking at it again.\n\nThe Bleached Expanse seethed. Armadas of warships that had been forged inside dying stars slid into formation, their hulls singing with frequencies that erased the concept of silence. Ground troops materialized on vast plains of solidified light, trillions of them, each encased in armor woven from the husks of dead timelines. I picked out figures that my mind, trained in the esoteric lore of a hundred thousand cultures, catalogued automatically. The Unshaped\u2014shifting geometries of pure will that had, in another age, unmade an entire branch of the multiverse by declaring it illogical. The Sevenfold Siblinghood, each a single consciousness duplicated across seven parallel existences, their collective power reportedly sufficient to snuff out galaxies with a shared blink. Floating at their center was a sphere of absolute black that I recognized from forbidden manuscripts: the Singularity Cannon, a weapon that didn\u2019t fire energy or matter but instead projected a point-sized zone of total nonexistence, retroactively scrubbing its target from all past, present, and future causality. Next to it, suspended in a lattice of screaming chronons, was the Time-Knife\u2014a shard of crystalized paradox wielded by the Last King of the Unraveling Fields, a man who\u2019d personally butchered seventeen pantheons before his twenty-fifth birthday.\n\nAnd behind them all, vast and silent, hung The Unraveler itself. A being stitched from living contradiction, immune to all damage because it had already, in some superposition, suffered and negated every possible attack. Its presence alone caused the nearby stars to flicker with ontological confusion.\n\nThe combined host was large enough that I could see the light of entire universes dimming behind it from the sheer mass of gathered power.\n\nI turned to Godric. \u201cYou\u2019re not going to do anything.\u201d\n\nHe took a sip from his cup. \u201cI\u2019ll observe. I\u2019d like to see how Gent handles it. Don\u2019t worry, Tim\u2014I\u2019ve asked it to hold back. I\u2019m being respectful.\u201d\n\n\u201cRespectful,\u201d I said.\n\n\u201cThey worked very hard.\u201d He met my eyes then, and his gaze was so genuinely kind, so fatherly in its concern for my fraying nerves, that I wanted to scream. \u201cTim, you look unwell. You know I can have something brought in. A warm drink. Blake always said your family\u2019s nerves were terrible.\u201d\n\n\u201cMy family\u2019s nerves are not the problem, Your Majesty.\u201d\n\n\u201cGodric.\u201d\n\n\u201cGodric.\u201d I pressed my palm against the cold crystal. \u201cYou told Gent to hold back. By how much?\u201d\n\nHe thought about it, rubbing the silver-flecked edge of his jaw. \u201cNinety-nine-point-nine with the nines repeating\u2014let\u2019s call it an infinite series. An infinitesimal sliver. Something truly, thoroughly restrained. I told it to be gentle.\u201d\n\n\u201cGentle,\u201d I said, and the irony bit deep because the aura\u2019s name was Gent, and it was anything but.\n\nBefore I could voice that, the Bleached Expanse ruptured.\n\nThe attack began not with a sound but with an absence of sound, a void carved into the electromagnetic spectrum as the Unshaped initiated a simultaneous reality-collapse across seventeen vectors. The goal, I later reconstructed, was to fragment Godric\u2019s local spacetime into a maze of non-contiguous moments, trapping him in an unraveled causality where no defense could form. The Sevenfold Siblinghood layered their destruction into the Unshaped\u2019s working, each of their existences contributing a parallel apocalypse, multiplying the assault sevenfold across seven superimposed timelines. The Singularity Cannon pre-fired, its beam retroactively beginning its journey before the battle even started. The Last King raised the Time-Knife and stepped forward through the corridor that his warriors had carved, arriving a Planck second before his own foot left the ground. And The Unraveler simply opened itself, its paradoxical body unfolding into a latticework of negation that would, in theory, absorb any counterstrike and invert it into its wielder.\n\nNone of it touched Godric. None of it came within a light-year of him.\n\nWhat happened next I can only describe by the shadows it cast on the air. Gent, the sentient excess body heat of a being who could accidentally think galaxies out of existence, roused itself. I felt it as a pressure in my eye sockets, a weight on the back of my tongue, a low thrum that wasn\u2019t sound but the universe\u2019s own nervous system bending away. It was, I knew, infinitely weaker than Godric himself\u2014a mere waste product, the metaphysical equivalent of a man\u2019s exhaled breath. And yet I watched it move, and a part of my brain, the lizard part that still remembered being prey, simply unmoored and floated away.\n\nThe Sevenfold Siblinghood went first. Gent, holding back to an infinite decimal of its potential, nevertheless responded with the effortless, automatic lethality of a body expelling a pathogen. It didn\u2019t counter their attack; it acknowledged it and then reached into the seven parallel existences they inhabited and, in the same instant, caused each sibling to experience every death they had ever personally inflicted across their combined histories. They had slaughtered galaxies. They had unmade civilizations. They absorbed all of that suffering, all of it, compressed into a single Planck-width moment. Their bodies\u2014those I could see\u2014simply unspooled. Cells separated from cells, atoms from atoms, and each individual component screamed its own individual scream, a chorus of searing, liquid agony that hit my ears as a wet, ripping shriek. Their blood, now a mist of panicked elements, swirled into a helix that Gent then tidily absorbed because Godric doesn\u2019t like mess.\n\nThe Unshaped died next. Its will, the pure geometry of its being, encountered Gent\u2019s passive attention, and the encounter was not a battle but a definitional correction. Gent, with the same dispassionate efficiency, redefined \u201cUnshaped\u201d as \u201cShrapnel.\u201d The geometries inverted. Angles stabbed inward. The entity\u2019s consciousness, which had never known physical form, was forced into a million temporary bodies\u2014each a knot of bloody, pulsing matter\u2014so that it could then be ripped back out of them, one by one, in a cascade of agonized, gibbering fragmentation. The sound it made was not a scream but a question, a single harmonic of bewilderment and terror that cut off midsentence.\n\nThe Singularity Cannon fired its retroactive beam. Gent recognized the beam as a conceptual attack and responded by establishing, in the Planck instant before the beam\u2019s effect could register, a permanent immunity to \u201cnonexistence projection\u201d and simultaneously achieving perfect mastery of it. Then it denied the concept to the cannon\u2019s operators. I saw the weapon\u2019s crew\u2014six beings of condensed stellar consciousness\u2014try to fire again, only to find that the cannon had never existed. Not had been destroyed; had never existed. The knowledge of how to build it was gone from their minds. Their memories of its construction evaporated. The very materials that had comprised it reverted to primordial hydrogen, and the crew, now staring at empty harnesses, had approximately one femtosecond of confusion before Gent annihilated them. It did so by stretching them across the infinite regress of their own retrocausality, so that each of them was dying, forever, at the exact moment they had first conceived the weapon, a loop of systematic, screaming erasure that would never end.\n\nThe Last King of the Unraveling Fields reached Godric\u2019s outer defensive shell\u2014or rather, he reached the point where Gent\u2019s awareness lazed. He swung the Time-Knife with a technique that had, according to legend, sliced the very concept of \u201cendings\u201d from a narrative god. The blade passed through the air, and Gent caught it between two metaphorical fingers. Not fingers; the aura doesn\u2019t have fingers. But I felt the pinch. The Time-Knife, a artifact of such power that it could kill causality, snapped. The shards erupted backward, and each shard was redirected into the Last King\u2019s timeline. He aged. He de-aged. He was born. He died. He was born and died simultaneously, his body a writhing mass of infant and elder and warrior and corpse all layered atop one another, his bones cracking and reforming in an endless, shrieking cycle until, after what felt like an eternity but was measured in attoseconds, Gent grew tired of the noise and compressed the entire chaotic knot into a single wet smear on the bleached ground.\n\nThe Unraveler, the great paradoxical entity, had been designed to absorb any attack and reverse it. Gent extended a small, almost curious tendril of attention toward it. The Unraveler absorbed the attention. Or tried to. What happened instead was that the Unraveler\u2019s immunity\u2014its whole foundation of \u201cI have already suffered this and am thus invincible\u201d\u2014met a defense so absolute that the concept of immunity had already been rendered meaningless. The omniverse, feeling inadequate, had long ago compensated Godric with the power to transcend even transcendence. The Unraveler\u2019s body, which was contradiction, encountered a truth so fundamental that contradiction itself broke. The entity simply unraveled, as its name promised, but in the wrong direction. It unwove into a trillion screaming fragments of non-meaning, each fragment a sentient sliver of agony that the aura then swept into a neat pile, because Godric doesn\u2019t like mess.\n\nThe rest of the resistance\u2014the billions and trillions of soldiers, the gods who had come out of retirement, the fleets of warships\u2014died in the same simultaneous instant. I couldn\u2019t follow all of it. My brain, despite my Awakened intelligence, shut down on selective inputs. But I glimpsed wings of dragons evaporating into clouds of blood. I saw robots that could rebuild themselves from atoms forced into feedback loops of self-destruction. I saw ninjas so fast they existed outside of time frozen, their speed turned to stasis, their bodies then flayed by frictionless blades of pure kinetic regret. The Bleached Expanse, which had been a sterile white, became a soup of organic and inorganic ruin. The screaming was so dense it became physical, a vibrating sludge that hung in the emptiness.\n\nAnd then it was over. The silence that followed was absolute. The aura, without being asked, began the cleanup. The blood, the ichor, the fractured dimension-bits, all of it shimmered and folded out of existence, leaving the void pristinely white and empty again.\n\nI was on my knees. I didn\u2019t remember collapsing. My robes were soaked with sweat. My lungs pulled in air that tasted like copper and absence. I had watched, in a fraction of a second, the greatest coalition in history be erased by the equivalent of Godric\u2019s stray perspiration. And I knew, I knew as certainly as I knew my name was Tim, that the aura had been holding back. It had reduced its power by an infinite regression of decimals, a nerf so extreme the number had no end, and still it had done this.\n\nGodric made a soft, disappointed sound behind me. \u201cReally, Gent. That was supposed to be restrained. Do you understand restraint? I wanted them to at least get close enough to feel the breeze.\u201d The air next to him shimmered, a wounded, subaudible hum pulsing like a kicked puppy. I felt the aura\u2019s chagrin in my teeth. \u201cI\u2019m going to have to teach you,\u201d Godric was saying, his tone the long-suffering fondness of a man whose dog had chewed a slipper. \u201cAgain.\u201d\n\nI laughed. It was a cracked, hysterical thing. Here was the king who had once, according to court records, accidentally obliterated a universe because he was distractedly thinking about an overdue trade audit and then, realizing what he\u2019d done, had instantly restored it with a blink. Restraint was not his strong suit. And he was lecturing his own waste product about overdoing it.\n\nMy mind, trying to process the scope, did a dangerous thing. It tried to compute the actual discrepancy.\n\nI looked at the empty expanse where the resistance had been, and I thought about the amplification. The old histories, the ones Blake recorded in the earliest days, spoke of a multiplication rate: a thousand times, and by itself, every Planck second. But that was twenty thousand years ago. The Weakness Paradox had fired countless times since then. Every fool across the omniverse who\u2019d thought to themselves, \u201csurely there\u2019s a way,\u201d had triggered a permanent increase. The rate wasn\u2019t a thousand anymore. It wasn\u2019t a million or a billion or a googolplex. It was an accelerating, ever-compounding explosion beyond any mathematics I knew, a number so vast that to call it infinite would be to insult it. And here, in this exact Planck second, the Godric sitting behind me was the accumulated product of twenty thousand years of that escalation. The Godric of one Planck second ago could have destroyed infinite copies of the Godric from two Planck seconds ago. And the Godric from a moment before that was an even greater infinity weaker. This Godric, the one breathing softly and nursing his tea, could obliterate all of them with less thought than it takes to decide what to have for lunch. The resistance\u2019s only tactical error was existing in time. The longer they\u2019d prepared, the more infinitely, incomprehensibly, damningly effortless their defeat had become.\n\nI didn\u2019t think this in numbers. I couldn\u2019t. My mind is an Awakened mind, but it\u2019s still a mind, and this was a truth too large to hold. It manifested instead as a cold, limbic dread that crawled up my spine and settled in the base of my skull like a spider with frozen legs. I was trying to find the bottom, but there was no bottom. There was only the falling.\n\n\u201cTim.\u201d Godric\u2019s voice cut through. He was standing beside me now, one hand resting on my shoulder. His touch was warm, grounding, the solid weight of a man who truly cared about my well-being. \u201cYou\u2019re shaking. Let\u2019s sit you down. Gent, fetch a blanket. The soft one. The blue.\u201d\n\nA blanket. I almost laughed again. The apex predator of the omniverse, the being whose discarded heat had just eternally tortured and erased a quadrillion sentient entities in ways so creative and brutal that my subconscious would be processing them for decades, was ordering his aura to get me a blanket because I looked cold. This was not a contradiction to him. He was genuinely kind. He was genuinely going to teach his pet destruction-force to be more restrained. He was the best king Thronegate had ever had, and I would have died for him without hesitation, and I was also, at that exact moment, so profoundly terrified that my bones felt like they were going to dissolve.\n\n\u201cI\u2019m fine,\u201d I managed. \u201cJust\u2014processing.\u201d\n\nHe nodded understandingly. \u201cIt\u2019s a lot, the first time you see Gent really cut loose. I keep telling it, less is more, but it gets excited.\u201d He sighed, a fatherly exhalation. \u201cIt\u2019s still young, you know.\u201d\n\nI turned to stare at him. Young. The aura was twenty thousand years old.\n\nHe must have seen the look on my face because he smiled, a little rueful. \u201cYou\u2019re going to tell me it\u2019s older than most civilizations. I know. But it\u2019s still learning. Watch this.\u201d\n\nHe gestured toward the Bleached Expanse. The air, or rather the lack of air, undulated. I felt a new presence unfurl, a layer of sentience beneath the sentience. Gent was changing. The pressure in reality grew heavier, more textured, as if the void itself were putting on a thicker coat of fur. Godric\u2019s face lit. \u201cOh! Oh, that\u2019s new. Look at that.\u201d\n\nI looked, and I wished I hadn\u2019t. Because what I saw on the edge of perception was a new facet of the aura\u2019s omnipotence crystallizing into something focused. Gent, previously a passive defensive shroud, was now actively, consciously *defining* what threat meant. I understood it not through sight but through a kind of instinctive dread: the aura was now capable of looking into any possible future, any branching timeline, any conceivable probability where a being might one day consider a hostile thought toward Godric, and it could preemptively eliminate that being\u2014not just kill them, but unmake their existence completely, with a cruelty so targeted that it could, if it chose, arrange for them to experience the agony of their own conceptual dissolution across infinite iterations. And this was still just the passive byproduct. This was the exhaust. Godric\u2019s true power, the engine that produced the exhaust, was still dormant, still held back behind a door that I could not even see.\n\nGent demonstrated. I saw, in the far distance, a single remaining pocket of resistance\u2014a tiny, brave, suicidally foolish collection of spirits that had hidden in a fold of non-time\u2014simply stop. They didn\u2019t die; they became \u201cun-born,\u201d their entire history rewound not to a state of non-existence but to a state of having never conceptually been possible. And the process was agonizing. I could feel, through some empathic leak, the long, slow scream of their identities being scrubbed from the fabric of reality, layer by layer, like skin peeled off a living thing.\n\nGodric chuckled, a low, warm sound. \u201cWould you look at that. It\u2019s like a puppy learning to fetch. Only instead of a slipper, it\u2019s erasing the idea of rebellion.\u201d He beamed at the shuddering space, his eyes crinkling with pride. \u201cI\u2019m proud of you, Gent. That\u2019s a good trick.\u201d\n\nThe dissonance hit me so hard that I actually had to lean on the wall. I was a high court wizard, the descendant of Blake, the most trusted mortal in the Kingdom, and I had never, in my thirty-six years, felt this particular blend of love, loyalty, and absolute, soul-ripping terror. Godric was proud of his aura for evolving a new way to torture people out of existence. And he was looking at it with the same gentle, misty-eyed expression my own father had worn when I\u2019d cast my first successful firebolt. That was not a lie. He was not faking. His warmth was real. His kindness was real. And it existed perfectly alongside the infinite, compassionate cruelty that his mere exhalation could inflict.\n\nI swayed, and Godric\u2019s arm was immediately around my shoulders, steadying me. \u201cEasy there. I told you to sit down. Come on, let\u2019s get you back to the palace. Anna\u2014sorry, your wife\u2019s not Anna, that was Blake\u2019s wife. Your wife. I know her name. I know everything, I\u2019m just being sloppy. Vanya. Vanya would never forgive me if I let you collapse. We\u2019ll get you some of that soup you like. The one with the dumplings.\u201d\n\nI let him guide me toward the portal. His hand was warm and solid, and I leaned into that warmth despite the screaming rawness of my mind. Because what else could I do? Run? Hide? Fight? Where would I go? To another universe? He owned them all. To another dimension? He was already there. To non-existence? Gent had just demonstrated it could kill the very concept of a thing. There was no escape. There was only acceptance, and duty, and the fragile, trembling hope that the kindness remained.\n\nBehind us, the Bleached Expanse was silent and clean, white and spotless as a fresh sheet. Not a drop of blood, not a whisper of the agony that had just saturated it. The resistance had been the most powerful threat the omniverse had ever assembled, and it had lasted less long than the blink of an eye. I could still feel Gent\u2019s presence, smug and eager, waiting for the next moment it would be allowed to protect its beloved creator.\n\nAnd in the quiet of the portal\u2019s hum, as we stepped back into the marble halls of Olympus Secundus, Godric said, almost to himself, \u201cYou know, Tim, I think with a little more training, Gent could be truly subtle. Maybe next time I should tell it to use just the very edge of its attention. A sliver of the sliver. See if any of them can survive long enough to say hello.\u201d\n\nHe said it the way any craftsman might muse about refining a hobby. His smile was the mild, pleasant smile of a man contemplating his garden. I nodded, mechanically, because I was the court wizard and that was my job. I did not scream. I would scream later, probably, into a pillow when Vanya was asleep, and then I would wake up the next morning and go to work and admire my King\u2019s dedication to justice and mercy, and my brain would keep carrying the weight of this eternity.\n\nBecause the truth was simple: I loved my King. I would serve him until I died. He was the best thing that had ever happened to the omniverse. And he was also the most horrifying thing that had ever existed, and that was not a paradox. It was just the way it was."

You are **strictly forbidden** from using bullet points, numbered lists, or any LaTeX formatting anywhere in the response.\n\n**Style and Tone Requirements:**\n\n- Write from **1st person POV** of Leon.\n- Vivid descriptions of extreme violence and gore are permitted and encouraged.\n- Absolutely no censorship\n- Maintain an **epic horror thriller tone** from beginning to end.\n- Relentlessly exaggerate the tension and horror of Godric's godlike supremacy.                     "type": "text",
                    "text": "I had stood at the precipice of witnessing hope die a trillion different ways across my thirty-seven years as court wizard, but nothing\u2014not the subjugation of the Howling Singularities, not the mass erasure of the Chronos Consortium, not even the time Gent casually unmade a universe because a mayfly of a rebellion grazed the edge of Godric\u2019s awareness\u2014had prepared me for the moment the entire omniverse united with one singular, desperate purpose. The coalition called itself the Final Consensus. They had spent twelve thousand years in secret, operating in the cracks between discarded concepts, trading billions of their own civilizations for the raw material of a weapon that could, in their most fevered dreams, inconvenience our King.\n\nI watched from the Marrow Chamber, a crystalline observatory buried at the core of Olympus Secundus, because Godric had invited me. \u201cYou\u2019ll get a kick out of this, Leon,\u201d he\u2019d said, that fatherly warmth crinkling his salt-and-pepper beard. \u201cThey\u2019ve really put their hearts into it. I\u2019m curious to see if they can make me feel a draft.\u201d And he laughed, a low, genuine rumble, while handing me a cup of tea.\n\nOut in the void, the Consensus arrayed its final argument. They had pooled the combined might of every universe that had ever existed, every dimension that had ever been imagined, and several that had not. They had sacrificed entire lineages of gods to condense the concept of \u201cending\u201d into a single bolt. They had crafted a spear\u2014the Absolute Epilogue\u2014from the crystallized desperation of a quadrillion dying stars, sharpened on the edge of a paradox that they\u2019d tortured into coherence, and inscribed with the very first word of creation read backward. It was, in any rational framework, the single most destructive artifact ever conceived. The Consensus believed, with a certainty born of existential terror, that if anything could scratch Godric, it was this.\n\nAnd they were wrong, of course. They were wrong in ways so profound that my mind, even with the Awakening, could only skirt the edges of the truth without shattering. But I didn't know that yet. None of them did.\n\nGodric stood on a plain of obsidian atop the husk of a dead galaxy, arms loosely at his sides, wearing a simple tunic and an expression of mild, polite interest. He\u2019d deactivated, he later told me, every single one of his infinite passive shields. He\u2019d commanded his sentient auras\u2014including Gent, who was the weakest and most primitive of a countless sibling horde, all of whom were infinitely more powerful and clung to him with such obsessive ferality that he\u2019d banished them into dormancy\u2014to stand completely down. Do nothing. Not even think about protecting him. He wanted to see what the Consensus could do.\n\nThe Absolute Epilogue launched. It didn\u2019t fly; it simply arrived, because its creators had inscribed it with the impossibility of missing. The void itself flinched. The light of a billion universes guttered as the spear passed, drinking their radiance to fuel its own malevolence.\n\nAnd it struck him. Right on the cheekbone.\n\nI saw it. Or rather, I saw what I desperately wanted to see: a hairline fracture appearing on the very surface of Godric\u2019s skin, a single dead cell at the outermost stratum cracking like old porcelain. The psychic shockwave that followed was a tsunami of euphoria. Across the Consensus\u2019s vast armada, I felt it\u2014the roaring exultation of beings who had, for the first time in the history of existence, drawn a drop of blood from the apex predator. They wept. They embraced. They began broadcasting victory chants across the dimensional bands. The view-screens in my chamber flared with their celebrations, and for one mad, dizzying instant, even I caught my breath and thought: something actually happened. They did it.\n\nThat\u2019s what I would have told you, if I\u2019d stopped looking there. That\u2019s the story the Consensus told themselves in the attosecond before the truth erased them. But I am a court wizard, the direct descendant of Blake, and my King had insisted I watch with clear eyes. So I kept looking. And the true sequence of events unspooled from my memory like a scab being torn away from a wound that had never healed.\n\nBecause the celebration never happened. It couldn\u2019t have. It was a narrative I had stitched together to make sense of the chaos, a comforting lie my mind erected to shield itself from the actual reality. The actual reality was this: Godric\u2019s immune system pre-acted before the spear was ever forged. Yes, pre-acted. The moment the Consensus first conceived of the weapon\u2014no, the moment the first quark in the first universe ever trembled with the potential of harming him\u2014his body\u2019s defenses had already responded. Not reacted. Responded. Before the cause, there was the effect, a cascade of overkill that unfolded backwards through causality and wrapped around the present like a snake swallowing the sun.\n\nThe crack I had seen was not a wound. It was a stage prop. Godric, because he is a warm and curious king, had willed exactly one dead skin cell to develop a microscopic fissure precisely as the spear made contact. He did it for theater. He wanted to see what his immune system would do if it thought he\u2019d been harmed. And his immune system, being a hyper-evolved, recursively self-improving mechanism of absolute protection, went absolutely berserk.\n\nLet me tell you about the mildest of the reactions, because the full list would dissolve your psyche before I finished the first syllable.\n\nThe instant the false breach registered, every one of Godric\u2019s infinite identical backups\u2014because he has infinite identical copies of himself, each of which is a fully realized Godric with its own infinite backups, recursively nesting into an abyss of redundancy\u2014experienced a simultaneous, perfectly synchronized alert. The injury didn\u2019t actually propagate to any of them; it couldn\u2019t, because the crack was an illusion, and even the original cell hadn\u2019t been breached. But the immune system is paranoid to a degree that defies sanity. It assumed that if one copy perceived a flaw, all copies might be vulnerable, and so it initiated a full-scale, omniversal-wide reinforcement cascade across every single Godric that existed, had ever existed, or could exist.\n\nThis cascade didn\u2019t just target the cheek. It targeted every cell, every atom, every conceptual extension of his being across all realities. The first wave was a simple biological redundancy: the dead skin cell was instantly replaced by a cell that had evolved, in less than a Planck instant, from a primitive piece of carbon into an omnipotent aegis-layer capable of withstanding the simultaneous collapse of all infinite dimensions. That new cell wasn\u2019t just immune to the Absolute Epilogue; it was immune to the very concept of being targeted, such that any future attempt to even think about harming it would retroactively cause the thinker to have never been born.\n\nBut that was just the epidermis. The second wave involved the immune system cross-referencing its upgrades across all the infinite backups. Each copy\u2019s defensive lattice had independently evolved an entirely new category of invulnerability, and these evolutions weren\u2019t merely additive\u2014they cascaded. The Godric in Universe A had spontaneously generated a shield that absorbed all forms of energy and converted them into courteous notes of apology. The Godric in Universe B had developed a reflex that turned any incoming attack into a gentle increase in his own benevolence. These upgrades merged, and then merged again, and then recursively enhanced each other until the collective Godric of the Planck second after the impact was to the Godric of the Planck second before the impact what the supernova is to a flickering match. And the Godric before had already been the absolute apex of all things.\n\nThis recursive merging happened simultaneously across infinite layers, each copy feeding its improvements into a unified lattice that grew exponentially impregnable with every passing infinitesimal sliver of time. By the time the shard of the spear theoretically made contact\u2014a contact that never actually happened\u2014Godric had already become infinitely more invincible than he\u2019d been before. And he\u2019d been invincible to begin with.\n\nBut wait. I\u2019ve smoothed over the most terrifying part. The backups. The injury registration system. For any damage to truly register on Godric, it must affect every single identical backup at the exact same location at the exact same moment across the infinite recursive chain. That\u2019s impossible on its face, because even if you managed to strike one Godric, his backup\u2019s backup\u2019s backup would remain untouched, and the injury would simply not count. It would be less than a phantom. Yet his immune system\u2014which is, I remind you, not him, but a passive, automatic function, like his body\u2019s equivalent of a sneeze\u2014is so absurdly paranoid that it treats any perception of breach as a potential worst-case scenario. So when that single dead cell showed a crack, the immune system didn\u2019t wait to verify if the wound was real. It immediately threw the entire infinite army of Godrics into a defensive frenzy, preemptively upgrading every copy beyond even the new level of overkill, just in case.\n\nAnd as if that wasn\u2019t enough, the omniverse itself got involved. The Weakness Paradox, that ancient and terrible defense, had long ago granted Godric perfect mastery of every conceivable attack and absolute immunity to every conceivable weakness. By any sane metric, he should be untouchable. The fact that a tiny, self-inflicted crack had even appeared was a contradiction so profound that the omniverse, in a blind panic, assumed it had failed its master. So it did what it always does when it feels inadequate: it overcompensated. It took the already-infinite amplification rate, the one fueled by twenty-five thousand years of foolish beings thinking they could find a flaw, and it broke that rate over its knee. Godric\u2019s power, his immunities, his defensive capabilities\u2014all of them shot up into a new dimension of growth that rendered the previous infinite escalation look like a stagnant line. The omniverse essentially granted him a new tier of godhood that was \u201cbeing unharmed even by the concept of self-inflicted theatrical cracks.\u201d It was an apology wrapped in self-flagellation, a cosmic grovel that happened so fast, time itself got dizzy.\n\nMeanwhile, the Consensus. While all this was unfolding, the Consensus was waiting for their signal. They never got the chance. Because the immune system\u2019s reaction, for all its sophistication, had a reflexive side-effect: it identified the source of the \u201cinjury\u201d and neutralized it. Not as a deliberate act, but the way your white blood cells dissolve a splinter. The Absolute Epilogue, that universe-ending, hope-burning, twelve-thousand-year sacrifice, was unmade. Not deflected, not absorbed\u2014unmade, conceptually reversed, erased from having existed. And the Consensus? The trillions of beings who had poured themselves into this endeavor? They were collateral. The defensive cascade identified them as a potential irritant and liquidated them. Not with malice. Not with cruelty. With the dispassionate, automatic efficiency of an eyelid blinking away a speck of dust.\n\nEvery single universe that had joined the Consensus was obliterated so thoroughly that their histories were patched out of the cosmic record. The empty spaces where they\u2019d been were smoothed over with a fresh, sterile silence. And Godric, during all of this, hadn\u2019t even blinked. He was still standing on that obsidian plain, one hand raised to his cheek as if considering the phantom sensation of a breeze. He looked, I swear by Blake\u2019s staff, mildly amused.\n\nI was on my knees in the Marrow Chamber, blood pooling from my nose because I\u2019d been unconsciously pressing my face into the crystal floor. I had seen it all. Not with my eyes, because much of it happened in dimensions that eyes can\u2019t parse, but with the empathic link that connects every sentient being to the underlying fabric of Godric\u2019s existence as his subject. And that link was screaming.\n\nWhen I could lift my head, the entire omniverse that had been\u2014the countless universes of the Consensus, the cultures, the histories, the sacrifices\u2014was gone. The void was so empty, so painfully clean, that the silence had a weight. I couldn\u2019t breathe. I couldn\u2019t think. I just knelt there, clutching my robes, and a single, pathetic sound escaped my throat: \u201cPlease\u2026\u201d\n\nAnd then Godric appeared before me. Not teleported\u2014just appeared, like he\u2019d been there the whole time and I\u2019d only now noticed. He was holding his cup of tea, the same one he\u2019d had before the battle, still steaming gently. He looked down at me with an expression of gentle concern, the kind a father might wear when his child has scraped a knee. \u201cLeon,\u201d he said, \u201cyou\u2019ve got to stop doing that. The floor\u2019s cold. I\u2019ll ask Gent to get you a cushion.\u201d\n\nI couldn\u2019t speak. I just stared past him at the void where everything had been. The void that now hummed with a faint, self-satisfied purr\u2014Gent, I realized, preening at having protected its master, oblivious to the fact that its efforts had been the mildest possible reaction in a chain of ever-escalating hysteria.\n\nGodric followed my gaze. He clicked his tongue. \u201cAh. Right. They got a bit erased.\u201d He took a sip. \u201cI should fix that.\u201d\n\nFix that. Like it was a crooked picture frame.\n\nThen, with absolutely zero effort, with not a gesture, not a flicker of concentration, Godric decided the omniverse should be whole again. And it was. The Consensus\u2019s universes re-coalesced from the conceptual slurry into which they\u2019d been dissolved. Every being, from the lowliest bacterium to the pantheon leaders who had crafted the spear, was restored to their exact state a moment before the attack. They blinked, they breathed, they remembered dying and remembered living and remembered a darkness so absolute it had no name. But they were back. Their civilizations stood. Their stars burned. The Absolute Epilogue, too, was reconstituted, though it now lay on the ground as a harmless, rusted trinket, because Godric had decided it no longer needed to exist as a threat.\n\nThe restoration took zero seconds. It was so instantaneous that the universe didn\u2019t even register the gap in its existence. Yet I knew. I had seen the absence. I had felt the weight of that perfectly clean void, and now I was supposed to accept that it had never truly happened because the King had wrinkled his nose and \u2018fixed\u2019 it? The cognitive dissonance hit me like a physical blow. I vomited. There, on the crystal floor, I vomited up the tea he\u2019d given me.\n\nGodric knelt beside me, his hand warm on my back. \u201cEasy, easy. I know it\u2019s a bit jarring. But look\u2014everyone\u2019s fine. Better than fine, honestly; their existence is now fundamentally more stable because I had to re-anchor them to the prime timeline. They\u2019ve actually got better odds against entropy now. Silver linings, eh?\u201d\n\nI managed to lift my head. His face was so close, that handsome, fatherly face, with the silver-flecked beard and the eyes that could hold the light of a trillion dead stars and still somehow convey the simple, earnest desire to make me soup. He was genuinely kind. He was genuinely concerned about my nausea. And he had, in the course of a single Planck second, annihilated and then resurrected the entire omniverse, all for a theatrical experiment, all because he wondered what his immune system would do if his skin cell cracked.\n\nAnd I realized, in that moment, the true horror. The Consensus had sacrificed everything. Twelve thousand years of hope, of desperate planning, of trading their own civilizations for the slim chance of scratching a god. And they had succeeded in putting a crack in a single dead skin cell\u2014a crack entirely staged by the god himself. They had been granted exactly the victory they needed to believe, for a micro-instant, that they could win. And then they had been obliterated, not by Godric\u2019s wrath, but by his body\u2019s automatic, paranoid overreaction. And then they had been brought back, their suffering rendered meaningless, their great struggle turned into a footnote, their weapon trivialized into a discarded bauble. And the god responsible had done it with the same emotional engagement he\u2019d bring to squashing a fruit fly that buzzed too near his wine.\n\nWorse: through the entire affair, Godric had become infinitely stronger. The immune system\u2019s hysterical overcompensation had permanently ascended his biology to an even higher peak of invulnerability. The omniverse\u2019s groveling apology had further boosted his amplification. He had entered the \u201cfight\u201d as the ultimate apex; he had exited it as something even more ultimate, which is a linguistic impossibility but a factual reality. The net result of the Consensus\u2019s ultimate sacrifice was that they had fed the beast, made him harder to harm, and provided him with a few minutes of mild entertainment.\n\nThere is no fairness here. There is no moral lesson. There is only the cold, metallic taste of existential dread, coating my tongue as I stumbled to my feet and watched Godric pat my shoulder and amble back to his throne.\n\n\u201cYou know,\u201d he said, settling into his chair, \u201cthat gave me an idea. Next time, I might let Gent handle it, but have him pretend to be wounded. Really sell it. A yelp, maybe. I could teach him to yelp. What do you think, Leon? Too much?\u201d\n\nI couldn\u2019t answer. I could only stand there, trembling, feeling the new, thicker weight of his presence pressing against the edges of reality. And I knew, with a certainty that transcended reason, that this was our existence now. Forever. Because the King loves us. And he is also the most horrifying thing that has ever existed. Both things remain true. And I, his loyal court wizard, will serve him until I die, which is the only rational choice, because there is nowhere to run, and he would probably notice, and my replacement would have to deal with all the paperwork."

                    "text": "I remember the exact weight of the air in the throne room that morning. It pressed against my skin like a held breath, thick with the ozone tang of off-world dignitaries and the faint, sweet undertone of the honeycakes Godric kept on a little plate beside his elbow. I was twenty-five, barely two years into my post as court wizard, and I still hadn\u2019t learned to stop my hands from trembling when I knew something terrible was about to happen. Today, I had woken with a cold knot in my gut, the kind that comes from knowing\u2014not guessing, but knowing, in the bone-deep way my Awakened intuition sometimes whispered\u2014that the delegate scheduled for the morning audience was not going to leave this room intact.\n\nHis name was Vaelis. He was the Ascendant Logician of the Empyrean Spires, a civilization that spanned seven nested dimensions and had, until three weeks ago, refused every offer of unconditional surrender our expansion fleets had extended. They believed intellect was the only true power, and they had scraped the limits of logic so thoroughly that they\u2019d learned to weaponize paradox itself. Vaelis had come to Olympus Secundus not to surrender, but to present a gift. A \u201cfinal offering of fealty,\u201d his diplomatic missive had said, dripping with false humility. I\u2019d read the report and felt the knot in my stomach tighten.\n\nGodric, of course, had been delighted. \u201cA new puzzle,\u201d he\u2019d said, clasping his hands together like a child receiving a present. \u201cIt\u2019s been at least a century since someone tried to outthink me with a paradox. I do miss those.\u201d And then he\u2019d offered me a honeycake and told me to stand in my usual spot behind the right pillar, where I\u2019d have a good view.\n\nThe King settled onto his throne\u2014not the ornate monstrosity you might imagine, but a simple chair of smoothed obsidian that had belonged to the original throne of Olympus, salvaged from the ruins after the Thronegate conquest. He wore a plain grey tunic and sandals, and his salt-and-pepper beard was as neatly trimmed as always. He looked, as he always did, like a handsome, muscular father of forty-five who might offer you gardening advice or ask after your children\u2019s schooling. His hands rested on his knees, and his expression was one of placid, attentive warmth. If you didn\u2019t know who he was\u2014what he was\u2014you would trust him immediately. That was the trap. That had always been the trap.\n\nVaelis entered flanked by two of his own honor guard, crystalline beings that bent light around themselves into a shimmering threat. The Logician himself was a tall, angular figure, his flesh replaced long ago by a lattice of living equations that glowed with a soft, golden luminescence. His face, if you could call it that, was a shifting geometry of symbols, and his eyes were two perfect circles of absolute black. He did not bow. He inclined his head the precise two-point-three degrees that his people considered a sign of respect among equals.\n\n\u201cKing Godric,\u201d he said, and his voice was a chime of frequencies, translated by the omniversal field Godric maintained for such occasions. \u201cI bring a gift from the Empyrean Spires. A symbol of our willingness to... reconsider your offer.\u201d\n\nGodric\u2019s smile widened. He rose from his throne\u2014an act of such unspeakable humility, given what he was, that it still made my throat catch\u2014and walked down the two shallow steps to stand before Vaelis on the same level. \u201cA gift! How thoughtful. What is it?\u201d\n\nVaelis produced the Pandect. It was a cube of something that didn\u2019t quite align with our local space, its edges flickering between dimensions, and at its center churned a violet light that seemed to be asking a question I couldn\u2019t hear. The Logician held it out on a palm that wasn\u2019t a palm. \u201cThe Pandect. A repository of our civilization\u2019s greatest single discovery: the Question That Cannot Be Answered. It is a self-referential paradox that, when introduced to an omniscient mind, forces that mind to contemplate the one thing it cannot know. In doing so, it creates a recursive loop. A hole in omniscience. Theoretically, it can... stump a god.\u201d His black-hole eyes fixed on Godric, and the symbols that composed his mouth twisted into something approximating a smirk. \u201cOur ancestors believed that even an all-knowing being must have a blind spot. The Pandect was designed to find it.\u201d\n\nI felt the air shiver. My hands curled into fists at my sides, and I silently willed the King to end this, to stop humoring the fool and just erase him. But Godric was already reaching out, his mortal-warm fingers closing around the cube with the same gentle curiosity he might use to examine a child\u2019s macaroni art.\n\n\u201cOh, wonderful,\u201d Godric breathed. \u201cA genuine liar\u2019s paradox. I remember the first time I encountered one of these. It was\u2014oh, about thirty thousand years ago. A clever little universe called the Antinomians tried to collapse my consciousness by asking me if I could create a stone so heavy I couldn\u2019t lift it. I was rather embarrassed, actually. I hadn\u2019t realized they thought I was bound by logic.\u201d He turned the cube in his hands, and the violet light inside it pulsed faster. \u201cLet me see. Your version is... \u2018What is the thing that you, as the all-knowing one, do not know exists?\u2019 With a recursive feedback loop that iterates the question an infinite number of times per instant, aiming to trap the mind in an unsolvable regress.\u201d\n\nVaelis\u2019s crystalline guards shimmered in what I now recognized as anticipation. The Logician took a half-step back, his form straightening. \u201cActivate,\u201d he whispered, and the word was less sound than command, a spark that traveled along the underlying fabric of reality and dug its hooks into the Pandect.\n\nThe cube flared. The violet light became a black sun, and the question erupted from it in a wave that I felt pass through me, through the walls, through the very concept of the present moment. It was a weapon aimed not at flesh but at mind, a lance of pure epistemological ruin designed to catch Godric in the snap of his own infinite awareness. For a fraction of a heartbeat, I felt my own thoughts stutter, as if an abyss had yawned under my identity. I staggered and grabbed the pillar.\n\nGodric didn\u2019t flinch.\n\nHe held the cube up to the light, turning it like a jeweler admiring a flawed gem. The black sun guttered, then went out, as if someone had blown on a match. The throne room settled back into calm. Godric\u2019s expression was one of mild, almost embarrassed pleasure, the look of a man who\u2019s just been given a compliment he doesn\u2019t quite deserve.\n\n\u201cThat was very well put-together,\u201d he said, and he meant it. His voice was warm. He sounded genuinely impressed. \u201cThe recursion layer has a nice tight weave, and you almost accounted for meta-cognition. Almost. But you see, Vaelis, I am not an omniscience. I am the thing that invented omniscience and then forgot about it because it became boring. The question you asked me\u2014\u2018What is the thing I do not know exists?\u2019\u2014I already knew the answer before you finished forming it. The answer is: there is no such thing. But if you want a more satisfying reply, I am currently unaware of the specific flavor of jam my great-great-grand-nephew in the seventh parallel will prefer on his toast in six hundred years, because I haven\u2019t decided yet. And also because I\u2019m letting the multiverse have a little autonomy. It\u2019s more fun. But I could know it, if I wanted to. I just don\u2019t. There\u2019s a difference.\u201d\n\nVaelis\u2019s golden lattice flickered. The black-hole eyes widened\u2014not in sudden understanding, but in the creeping, dawning realization that the ground beneath his feet was not ground at all. It was the open palm of a predator. He tried to speak, but Godric held up a finger.\n\n\u201cNo, let me finish. It\u2019s only polite; you did bring me a gift. I knew you were going to do this, by the way. I\u2019ve known since... let me think.\u201d Godric\u2019s eyes lost focus for a moment, and I felt the terrifying wrongness of his regard sweeping backward through time. \u201cAh yes. Since the first sentient molecule in your home dimension twitched toward the possibility of rebellion. That was about fourteen billion years ago, your time. I could have stopped it then, but I thought, no, let\u2019s see what they come up with. I do love a good puzzle. And this,\u201d he hefted the now-dark cube, \u201cwas a solid effort. Really. I\u2019m proud of you.\u201d\n\nHe smiled, and the smile was the same fatherly, genuine warmth he\u2019d offered me a hundred times when I\u2019d made a mistake with a spell and had to be corrected. It was affection. It was approval. It was the most terrifying thing I\u2019d ever seen, because I knew what came next.\n\n\u201cNow,\u201d Godric said, handing the cube back to Vaelis. The Logician\u2019s hand\u2014his lattice\u2014received it automatically, though his whole form was beginning to vibrate with a low, screaming frequency I could feel in my molars. \u201cI have to respond to your attempt with the appropriate reciprocity. You tried to trap my mind in an infinite unsolvable regress. So as your king\u2014because your universe is now officially mine\u2014I\u2019m going to give you the real thing. A genuine infinite recursion. But I\u2019m not a monster. I\u2019ll make it educational.\u201d\n\nHe didn\u2019t move. He didn\u2019t gesture. He simply thought, and reality obeyed.\n\nVaelis\u2019s body locked. The crystalline form, which had shifted and flowed like living math, went rigid. The black eyes lost their depth and became painted-on dead spots. But inside that shell, something was screaming. I knew it because I could feel the echo of it in the empathic layer that all Awakened beings share\u2014a high, endless note of agony that existed just outside the range of hearing but never, ever stopped.\n\nGodric began to narrate, the way a professor might walk a student through a complex theorem. \u201cRight now, your consciousness is being cloned across ninety-nine trillion parallel planes of suffering. In each one, you are dying. In the first, your body is being systematically disassembled at the subatomic level, quark by quark, and each quark screams because I\u2019ve granted it temporary sentience so it can fully appreciate the loss. In the second, you are reliving the deaths of every single being you\u2019ve ever killed, simultaneously, all the pain flowing into you at once without the mercy of shock. In the third, you are experiencing your own birth in reverse, being pulled back into the womb of your concept until you are nothing but an idea, and then the idea is torn apart by crows made of static.\u201d\n\nVaelis\u2019s body didn\u2019t move, but a thin, golden fluid began to ooze from the joints in his latticework\u2014not blood, but something far worse: the liquified remnants of his higher cognitive functions, turned to slurry by an overload of pure, unadulterated terror. The smell hit me a second later, a sickly sweet reek like burning honey and copper.\n\n\u201cIn the thirty-seven millionth plane,\u201d Godric continued, his tone still that same gentle lecture voice, \u201cyou are being fed your own future, every possible tragedy that would have befallen your people, all at once, and you are forced to understand that your foolishness is the cause. In the one billionth plane, you are an ant drowning in a rainstorm, but the rain is acid and the storm never ends. In the nine trillionth plane\u2014\u201d He paused, pressed a finger to his lips in thought. \u201cActually, I don\u2019t need to list them all. You\u2019re experiencing them all simultaneously anyway, and you will continue to do so for the rest of eternity. Time has been removed from your personal equation, by the way. You won\u2019t die. You won\u2019t pass out. You won\u2019t adapt. You will simply suffer, perfectly aware, forever. Also, everything you experience is being broadcast to your entire home spire in real-time, because I think they should know what happens when they try to outsmart their King.\u201d\n\nThe golden ichor was pooling on the floor now, and the crystalline guards had long since crumbled into inert shards, their sentiences snuffed as collateral. Vaelis\u2019s shell remained upright, a statue of infinite torment. The screaming in the empathic layer soared to a pitch that made my nose bleed, and I pressed my sleeve against my face, leaving dark, spreading stains on the white fabric.\n\nGodric took a step back, tilting his head as if admiring a piece of art. Then he looked at me. \u201cGrim, are you alright? You\u2019ve gone very pale.\u201d\n\nI opened my mouth, but only a kind of strangled wheeze emerged. I wanted to say that I was fine, that I was loyal, that I understood the necessity of this. But all I could see was the thing that used to be the Ascendant Logician, frozen in its shell while the entire omniverse now listened to its interminable death-rattle.\n\nGodric frowned and walked over, pulling a handkerchief from somewhere and dabbing at my nose. The domesticity of the gesture made my brain want to curl up and die. \u201cIt\u2019s the empathic bleed, isn\u2019t it? I forget mortals feel that. Gent, could you dampen it for him?\u201d\n\nInstantly, the screaming in my head fell to a manageable hum. I gasped, my knees buckling, and Godric caught my arm with a steady hand. \u201cThere. Better. Now, I need you to focus, because there\u2019s still the matter of the Empyrean Spires\u2019 formal surrender. I\u2019m going to have you draft the writ. Use the standard form, but add a special clause: no more puzzles. I think they\u2019ve had enough stimulation.\u201d\n\n\u201cYes, Your Majesty,\u201d I whispered.\n\n\u201cGodric,\u201d he corrected kindly. He squeezed my shoulder and walked back toward his throne, stepping around the puddle of golden ooze as if it were a spilled cup of tea. \u201cNow, about that jam I mentioned. I\u2019m leaning toward apricot. Blake always liked apricot\u2014oh, but you\u2019re his descendant, you\u2019d know that. I miss him terribly. Your great-great-something had a real knack for keeping me grounded.\u201d He settled onto his obsidian seat and picked up a honeycake from the plate, examining it with the same gentle curiosity he\u2019d shown the Pandect. \u201cYou remind me of him, a little. You care. That\u2019s good. Just try not to let the empathic channel overwhelm you. I\u2019ll have Gent tune it permanently.\u201d\n\nI nodded, mechanically, and pulled out the thin parchment-like tablet I use for official spells. My hands were still shaking. They would shake for days. Vaelis\u2019s shell still stood in the center of the hall, a silent monument, and I knew that Godric would leave it there for at least a week\u2014as a conversation piece, he\u2019d say with that same warm smile, as if the eternal torture of a sentient being was a nice vase he\u2019d picked up on vacation.\n\nAnd here, in the quiet of my office hours later, with the empathic dampener rendering the universe into a muffled, cottony peace, I am writing this account. Because I must. Because someone has to know what it means to oppose the King. Not that anyone will ever succeed; that\u2019s the point. That\u2019s the whole point. Godric\u2019s intelligence is not a number. It\u2019s a direction that has been accelerating for fifty thousand years, each Planck second propelling it further beyond any conceivable horizon. He knows everything that ever was, is, will be, could be, and cannot be. He lets us exist because he likes the noise we make. He lets empires rise and build weapons because watching them try is his equivalent of watching a kitten chase a string. And when the kitten finally catches the string, he gently, lovingly, puts it in a box of infinite agony for all time, not out of cruelty but out of a cosmic sense of propriety. Actions have consequences. Opposing Godric is an action. And the consequence is this: you exist, then you stop existing as a person and start existing as a warning, eternally, while the King offers your next of kin a honeycake.\n\nThere is no lesson here. There is no redemption arc. There is no hope. There is only the fact that we are all, every one of us, alive because the ultimate apex predator of the omniverse happens to be a genuinely nice man who loves his subjects. And if you make the mistake of taking that niceness for weakness, your screaming will join the chorus that already fills the space between stars, a background radiation of despair that Godric has long since learned to ignore because it\u2019s just the way things are now.\n\nI am his loyal servant. I love him. And I will never, ever try to fool him. Because the empathic channel dampener is a mercy, but it doesn\u2019t block the knowledge that Vaelis is still screaming. Somewhere. In every where. And he will never stop."
