                    "type": "text",
                    "text": "I have served the King since I could hold a wand. My earliest memory is of sitting on Uncle Godric\u2019s knee in the palace gardens, a child of five, while he pointed out constellations and told me which ones he\u2019d accidentally extinguished before I was born. I remember his laugh, a low, rolling rumble, and the way his salt-and-pepper beard tickled my forehead when he hugged me. He was Uncle Godric to me long before he was \u201cYour Majesty\u201d or \u201cthe apex\u201d or any of the titles the rest of the omniverse whispered with wet-throated dread. He was the warm, smiling pillar of my world, and because he never cast a single spell in my presence, I assumed it was because he couldn\u2019t. That was the family tradition, wasn\u2019t it? Every king needed a court wizard. My great-great-great-something-grandfather Blake had been the first, and ever since, the eldest child of our line with magical talent took the post. It was our sacred duty to protect the Crown with our arcane skill, and I, Gorm, the latest in that lineage, had just turned twenty and received my staff. My father had told me, voice thick with pride, that my magic was the strongest our bloodline had produced in centuries. Every day past twenty, the Awakening amplified that strength tenfold\u2014or in our family\u2019s unique inheritance, a thousandfold. By the time I was thirty, I would be capable of sundering galaxies. I was certain I would be the shield Uncle Godric needed. Because surely, if he had magic of his own, he would have used it. Surely.\n\nThis belief was the foundation beneath my feet. It took one morning to reduce it to ash.\n\nThe attack came during the Feast of the Ninth Concord, an annual celebration marking the subjugation of a particularly stubborn universe whose name I\u2019ve since forgotten. The marble halls of Olympus Secundus were thronged with dignitaries from across the conquered cosmos, their varied bodies wearing expressions of careful, practiced reverence. I stood at Godric\u2019s right hand, my new staff humming with energies I had spent weeks weaving into protective wards around the dais. Uncle Godric lounged on his simple obsidian chair, dressed in a blue tunic that had a small gravy stain from breakfast, and he chatted with a delegate from the Ash-Colored Nebula about the best way to grow tomatoes in zero-gravity. He looked so ordinary, so profoundly mortal, that my resolve hardened. I would protect him. I was ready.\n\nThe assassination attempt came not from the crowd but from the very fabric of the hall. The ceiling, which had been a tranquil illusion of a starfield, tore open like a wound, and through the rift descended a shape I recognized from forbidden grimoires: a Remnant Ascendant, a being that had once been a pantheon of twelve fused magic-users who had transcended even the concept of transcendence. It was a thing of whirling, angular light and searing black tendrils, its body a walking paradox that had, according to legend, unknit the First Loom of Creation before being sealed outside reality. How it had pierced Thronegate\u2019s defenses, I didn\u2019t know. Later I would learn Godric had allowed it, had held his auras back and deactivated his shields down to the most infinitesimal layer, because he wanted to see what I would do. But at that moment, all I felt was a surge of protective fury.\n\nI launched every spell I had. A bolt of unbound chronons that could age a star to dust. A lattice of binding sigils that had once held a mad universe-eater in stasis for a millennium. A cascade of ontological erasure that, I had been taught, could unmake any entity that dared exist in opposition to the Crown. My staff blazed with white-hot light, and the air in the hall screamed as my magic tore through it. The Remnant Ascendant didn\u2019t even slow. It brushed my projections aside with a flex of its tendrils, the way a man might swat a moth, and I felt the recoil hit me like a collapsing wall. My nose burst with blood, my head snapped back, and I stumbled, my staff skittering across the floor. The dignitaries were fleeing, some on fire, others simply evaporating from the mere presence of the attacker. I tried to rise, to put myself between the thing and my king, but my legs were jelly and my magic was a guttering flame.\n\nGodric, still seated, took a sip from his cup of wine. He didn\u2019t look up. He didn\u2019t set the cup down. He simply exhaled through his nose, the faintest sound of mild irritation, and then did nothing.\n\nBut nothing, for Godric, is a word that has no meaning.\n\nWithout a gesture, without a word, without even a flicker of concentration, a thread of his magic unfurled into the hall. I knew it was magic because my family has an inherited sensitivity to arcane forces, and what I felt in that instant was so far beyond anything I had ever encountered that my brain, in sheer self-defense, initially named it as a failure of my senses. It wasn\u2019t a spell. It wasn\u2019t an incantation. It was less than an afterthought\u2014a fraction so infinitesimal that I could only compare it to the way a sleeping giant\u2019s smallest exhalation might disturb a single mote of dust. And yet that fraction, that practically-zero-percent of Godric\u2019s true magical capacity, contained enough power to erase the entire omniverse infinite times over.\n\nI know this because he told me so, later, but in that moment I felt it. The thread of his magic, which was not even a thread but more the concept of a thread, touched the Remnant Ascendant. And the Ascendant, the being that had shrugged off my strongest attacks as if they were poetry recitations, experienced something that no description can truly capture. Its angular light extinguished in a way that wasn\u2019t extinguishing but rather anti-ignition, a reversal of existence that began at the very first moment of its conception and rewound forward simultaneously, so that every Planck instant of its being was being unmade in parallel across all its timestreams. The black tendrils froze, then fibrillated, then began to weep a thick, purple ichor that was not blood but the liquefied remains of its deific authority. The sound it made\u2014a sound I will carry into my grave, though I pray for a grave\u2014was not a scream. A scream implies a throat, lungs, the need for air. This was a vibration in the raw substrate of consciousness, a broadcast of pure, undiluted agony that bypassed my ears and carved itself directly into the marrow of my soul. The Ascendant\u2019s body, if that shifting geometry could be called a body, began to fold in on itself. But it was not a simple implosion. Godric\u2019s magic, that negligible wisp, was deconstructing it layer by metaphysical layer. First, it unmade the Ascendant\u2019s mastery over time, so that the entity was forced to experience every death it had ever inflicted upon others\u2014a trillion, trillion sentient beings\u2014all at once, in a recursive loop that stretched each individual agony into an infinite duration within a single attosecond. Then it unmade the Ascendant\u2019s mastery over space, so that its scattered, screaming parts were simultaneously compressed into a point smaller than a quark and expanded across a billion light-years of vacuum, existing in both states at once, a paradox of dismemberment that never resolved. The ichor that sprayed from the process splattered the walls, the floor, the throne itself, and where it landed it hissed and ate through marble and crystal, releasing fumes that smelled like roasted honey and fresh copper. The dignitaries who hadn\u2019t escaped died on their feet, their bodies simply giving up their hold on life as their minds overloaded on the empathic backwash of the Ascendant\u2019s suffering. I was on my knees, vomiting, my eyes burning, my own magic shriveling inside me like a frightened animal.\n\nAnd through all of this, Godric\u2019s expression was one of mild, distant consideration. He took another sip of his wine, then looked down at the gore that had spattered his tunic. \u201cHonestly,\u201d he murmured, and his voice was the same warm, fatherly rumble it had always been. \u201cI just had this cleaned.\u201d\n\nHe lifted a finger. Not to cast a spell\u2014he didn\u2019t need to. The thread of magic, that still-lingering wisp, flexed once more, and the Ascendant\u2019s unmaking entered a new phase. Because Godric, as I now understood, hadn\u2019t merely destroyed it. That would have been a mercy, and Godric, to those who oppose him, does not offer mercy. The Ascendant\u2019s consciousness, its very selfhood, was being preserved and tormented across an infinite regression of collapsing realities. I saw, through the empathic link, flashes of its eternal fate: it would be repeatedly reborn into new, weaker forms, each one a different flavor of helpless prey, and in each life it would be hunted, cornered, and eaten alive by a predator that reflected its own original arrogance. A billion cycles of this had already passed in the space between heartbeats, and the number of cycles still to come was a figure with more zeroes than the total count of atoms in the omniverse. And it would remember every single one. It would remember the taste of its own flesh in alien mouths, the feel of its bones snapping under alien claws, the cold, eternal dark of dying hopeless and alone, over and over, forever. This was not punishment. This was the natural, automatic consequence of having dared to raise a hand against the King of Thronegate. This was simply how the universe worked now.\n\nThe Ascendant\u2019s final wail faded into a subsonic hum. The hall fell silent. A few surviving dignitaries lay groaning in corners. The walls dripped with viscera and melting architecture. And Godric turned to me, his eyes crinkling with that same uncle-warmth I\u2019d known all my life. \u201cGorm,\u201d he said softly. \u201cAre you hurt?\u201d\n\nI couldn\u2019t speak. My jaw worked, but only a thin, keening whimper escaped. He frowned, set down his cup, and moved to kneel beside me. His hands, those same hands that had tousled my hair when I was a child, lifted my chin. \u201cLet me see. You\u2019ve got a nosebleed. Did the back-blast catch you? I should have dampened it. I forget mortals are so fragile.\u201d He produced a handkerchief from nowhere and pressed it gently to my face. His touch was gentle. Caring. It was the most terrifying thing I had ever felt.\n\nFor a long moment, I just let him tend to me, my mind a white, screaming blank. Then, with a voice that sounded like a stranger\u2019s, I rasped, \u201cYou have magic.\u201d\n\nHe paused. The concerned frown on his face eased into a faint, knowing smile. \u201cOf course I do, my boy. I have everything.\u201d\n\n\u201cBut you never\u2026\u201d\n\n\u201cI never use it because there\u2019s no need. And because it\u2019s more fun to watch you practice. Your family has served me as wizards for eighty thousand years, Gorm. Do you really think I needed a court wizard?\u201d He chuckled, a low, affectionate sound. \u201cYour great-grandfather Blake was my best friend. I kept him close not because he could shield me from anything\u2014though he tried, poor man, he tried so hard\u2014but because I loved him. I love all of you. You\u2019re my family. The magic is just\u2026 a hobby we share.\u201d\n\nThe foundation of my identity crumbled. I had spent my entire life believing I was the protector. The shield. The sword. I had just watched a being that could unknit creation be erased, tortured, and eternally damned by a wisp of my king\u2019s idle thought, and I understood, with a clarity that felt like being flayed, that my strongest spell, my most potent working, the absolute peak of my thousandfold-amplified magical lineage, was to that wisp what a single grain of sand is to the entire mass of all the universes combined\u2014an insultingly insufficient comparison, because the gap was not measurable in magnitudes. It was not a gap at all. It was a category error. I had tried to add a candle flame to a supernova, believing I was brightening the light.\n\nGodric helped me to my feet, steadying me as my legs wobbled. \u201cThere now. Deep breaths. You did very well, by the way. That chronon bolt would have annihilated a lesser entity. You should be proud. I\u2019m proud of you.\u201d\n\nProud. He was proud of me. The word scraped across my nerves like a rusty blade. Before I could respond, he turned back to the ruined hall, and with a flick of his finger, the same thread of magic\u2014still less than a whisper, still that practically-zero-percent of his full capacity\u2014swept outward. The gore on the floor shimmered and vanished. The dead dignitaries gasped and sat up, their wounds gone, their clothes pristine, their memories of their own deaths intact but rendered somehow distant, like a half-forgotten nightmare. The melted walls flowed back into their original forms. The starfield illusion reasserted itself. A moment later, the palace chamber was exactly as it had been before the attack, except for the faint scent of ozone that clung to the air and the new cowering posture of everyone present.\n\nAnd the Remnant Ascendant? It was gone, as if it had never been. But I knew, with an instinct born of the Awakening, that it was not gone. It was somewhere. It would always be somewhere, screaming, and that somewhere was woven into the very fabric of this restored hall like a hairline crack in a mirror\u2014invisible, but permanent. Godric had not just killed it. He had made it a lesson. A monument.\n\nI think he sensed my thoughts, because he placed his hand on my shoulder and leaned in close, his beard brushing my ear. His voice dropped to a murmur, still warm, still kind, but carrying a weight that I felt in my bones. \u201cThe truth is, Gorm, that there has never been anything in the entire omniverse that could threaten me. Not before you were born, not now, not in all the infinite eons to come. The moment anyone even dreams of opposing me, they\u2019ve already lost. They just don\u2019t know it yet. The magic you saw me use? That was less than a speck. It was the equivalent of me clearing my throat. If I ever used even a real fraction of my full power\u2014if I ever had a reason to\u2014there would be nothing left to save. So I don\u2019t. I hold back. I let beings like that Ascendant crawl out of their holes and take their best shot.\u201d He smiled, and the smile was the same one he\u2019d worn when I was a child and he\u2019d taught me to skip stones across a lake. \u201cIt\u2019s only fair.\u201d\n\nHe gave my shoulder a final squeeze, then released me and turned to address the trembling assembly, his voice lifting into the cheerful, fatherly boom he used for public addresses. \u201cApologies for the interruption, everyone! A small technical difficulty. Please, enjoy the feast. The roast has been respawned and the wine is fresh. Let\u2019s have no more unpleasantness.\u201d\n\nThe crowd, conditioned by decades or centuries or millennia of Godric\u2019s rule, began to unclench. Laughter, hesitant at first, then more genuine, echoed off the rebuilt marble. Music started up again. Servants appeared with platters of meat and fruit. The Feast of the Ninth Concord resumed, and no one spoke of what had happened. No one dared. The cognitive dissonance was a survival mechanism, and I watched it take hold of the room like a drug.\n\nI stood off to the side, my staff retrieved but my hands glued to its haft by drying sweat. I watched Godric move through the crowd, clapping backs, praising a delegate\u2019s new offspring, dipping his finger into a sauce and smacking his lips with a homely satisfaction. I watched him laugh, a full, genuine belly-laugh at some joke a terrified underling told. And I watched the space where the Ascendant had been, a space that now thrummed with a silent, eternal scream that only I seemed to hear.\n\nMy belief was gone. My purpose was gone. In its place was a cold, rigid horror that had no name. I was the court wizard to a being who did not need, had never needed, and would never need my protection. My entire ancestral purpose was a comforting lie, a gift Godric had given us because he liked having friends. And the gratitude I felt for that\u2014because I did feel gratitude, because I loved him, because he was the only uncle I\u2019d ever known\u2014mixed with the existential dread until I couldn\u2019t tell them apart. They were the same feeling, now. They would be the same feeling for the rest of my life.\n\nLater that night, after the feast wound down and the guests were ushered away, I stood alone in the rebuilt hall. The empathic link that all of Blake\u2019s line carries was clearer now than ever, and I could feel the Ascendant\u2019s torment still resonating in the sub-quantum fabric, a permanent fixture of the room\u2019s aura. I knelt and touched the floor where the creature had first appeared. My fingers came away cold, with a faint static tingle, and I heard, for just an instant, the faint echo of a scream.\n\n\u201cBest not to dwell on it,\u201d said a voice behind me.\n\nI spun. Godric stood a few feet away, a cup of warm milk in his hands\u2014his bedtime drink. He looked sleepy and content, the way any normal father might after a long party. \u201cThat bit of floor will always be a little haunted, I\u2019m afraid. I could clean it up completely, but I like to leave reminders. It\u2019s good for morale.\u201d\n\nI stared at him. \u201cMorale?\u201d\n\nHe nodded, taking a sip of his milk. \u201cMy people need to know, somewhere deep in their bones, that opposing me is the worst possible thing they can do. Not because I\u2019m cruel\u2014I\u2019m not, you know I\u2019m not\u2014but because the universe itself won\u2019t tolerate it anymore. It\u2019s safer for everyone if the lesson is clear. The suffering of one or two or a trillion idiots is a small price for eternal peace, don\u2019t you think?\u201d\n\nHe said it the way a man might discuss crop rotation. Practical. Kindly. Utterly, irrevocably sincere.\n\nI didn\u2019t answer. Couldn\u2019t.\n\nHe smiled, that same fatherly smile, and patted my cheek. \u201cGet some sleep, Gorm. Tomorrow we\u2019ll work on that binding sigil you attempted. It was a bit loose around the edges. I\u2019ll show you how to tighten it. I don\u2019t need a court wizard, but I do like having one. It\u2019s tradition. And you\u2019re family.\u201d\n\nThen he walked away, his soft footsteps echoing on the marble, and I was left alone with the silent scream of the thing that had thought it could challenge him. The scream that would continue for all eternity because the King had forgotten to turn it off, or maybe because he preferred the ambience. I didn\u2019t sleep that night. I sat in my room with my staff across my knees, and I listened to the hum of the universe, and I understood, with a finality that left no room for doubt, that there is no opposing Godric. There is only obedience, or agony without end. And the agonizing part is that he genuinely cares for us. That his kindness is real. Because knowing that makes the horror inescapable. It means we could never band together to overthrow a monster, because he is not a monster. He is a good man, a good king, a good uncle, and he will feed your soul to a recursive nightmare if you try to hurt his family. And he\u2019ll do it while asking about your children\u2019s education.\n\nI am his loyal servant. I will always be his loyal servant. And the foundation of my world has been replaced by an abyss, and I am falling into it, and I do not think I will ever stop."
